We have chosen to stay in the garden lanai, a separate building from the tower because it is quieter than the rooms in the main building. The room is larger with a balcony overlooking gorgeous vegetation. The down side is some of the rooms on the first floor have jacuzzis and if the guests want to, they can stay out on their balcony using the jazucci and the sound does travel (although I am certain that is not their intention). The restaurants in this hotel are fantastic and guests from other hotels come here to use the casino. The Palm (steak), Yamato (Japanese) and Brother Jimmy's BBQ on the roof are all fantastic. We went to Koco for dessert one night (they have their own pastry chef) which was more than fantastic. We tried eating there Friday night but they were having a private party. The pizza place is not New York Pizza, sadly. There is live music in the majestic lobby Thursday and Friday nights with people from the island coming in to dance. What fun to watch! Yvonne Ramos, the Front office Assistant manger, handled any of our inconveniences professionally and to our utmost satisfaction. The gym is state of the art. There were free yoga classes offerred outside between the hotel and the pool shed. We stayed a week and were sorry to leave. To all the workers and everyone we met at the El San Juan: Prospero Ano Nuevo.

<Author>keithd18
<Content>Great Stay Stayed at the El San Juan hotel for 4 nights. The trip to the hotel is $22 by taxi and takes 5-10 minutes. Hotel: The hotel is very close to the airport but you do not see planes taking off and landing. Had a regular room, which was fine. The bathroom is very small and there are no balconies. Most of the rooms are not on the beach; you could see the ocean from our room if you looked to the left. There is a 24-hour supermarket down the street that has everything you need. The Supermarket is in a plaza that has a bank, a curves and a pharmacy. The supermarket sells all kinds of liquor, beer, and wine. We bought liquor and carried it into our room. The casino is small and deals blackjack abnormally, which gives them an additional edge. We went to the Ritz and played in their casino, its much larger, has more games, you can walk there or take a short cab ride. At night the hotel has live entertainment in the lobby. The drinks at the hotel are very expensive, $8 beers, $10 rum and cokes, $12 pool drinks, etc. Food:We had breakfast at Starbucks, which is in the lobby. For lunch we found a Mexican/Spanish restaurant next door to the hotel that is owned by Ed Figueroa (first PRican to win 20 games in the major leagues, played for the 78 Yankees) and had great lunches there. For dinner we ate at The Palms in the hotel that was great as usual. We ate at a place called Risces in Old San Juan that was great (15 min cab ride) and a place down the street next to Burger King and across from the Intercontinental called Mi Casa (that may not be the whole name but its Mi something, has a white sign). Everything we ate was excellent. We also went to the rooftop bar/restaurant at the El San Juan called Brother Jimmy's, they had great bar food (wings, quasadillas, etc). Pool:The pool is really nice; there are 2 main pools with plenty of seats. There is a swim up bar that opens around 11. The beach is nice also; it鈥檚 public so you can bring your own alcohol. Weather: The weather was perfect for 3 out of 4 days. One of the days it rained on and off for much of the day, the other days were sunny and very hot. There was a 6.1 magnitude earthquake when we were there, the hotel shook, but everyone was ok.Overall:The only thing I can think of that I didn鈥檛 like was the smoking rules; you can鈥檛 smoke anywhere except the beach or outside the front door. No smoking at the pool, in your room or the casino. This is a positive for most but if you like to smoke a cigar its somewhat of an inconvenience. Everyone we spoke to was from NY/NJ or Boston so it was a good crowd (besides the Red Sox fans). The next time I go to PR I will stay at the El San Juan Hotel because its convenient, and the food is great.

<Author>pjs-MA
<Content>Good and Bad at the same time... We recently returned from a long weekend stay at the El San Juan Hotel and Casino. I had read many reviews prior to booking and researched other resorts as well. I have to say I found the reviews to be right on the money and knew what to expect ahead of time. The hotel is located close to the airport so great for a quick get away where you do not want to waste time in route to your hotel- I only actually heard an airplane overhead on one occasion-not an issue... The lobby is gorgeous and definitely comes alive at night and is a great place to be, enjoy yourself and have fun- probably one of the best features of this hotel! Also, we ate at two of the restaurants for dinner- the Sushi one which was very good, but the one that sticks out the most is Kocco's- unbelievably great food and service- the best service we had all weekend. It was quite surprsing since the pool sevice (for food) was extremely slow, we were expecting the same situation for dinner. On a side note, they are also run by the same management that runs Dragonfly in Old San Juan which was also an outstanding meal and great service!!Now for the rooms- definitely disappointing. The hallways had a musty odor to them, it could be because thay had a lot of rain that week prior to my arrival. The bed was comfortable, TV was good, but the bathroom was bad! It was not clean at all. The floor was dirty and the toilet was clearly not cleaned completely in some time- without going into detail about it, it was obvious. The shower curtain was white and the bottom of it was blackened with mold and the tiles were very grungy looking. The bathroom needs to be remodeled badly! The pipes under the very tiny sink were all rusty as well. I can't imagine seeing that at the Ritz! (which was my 2nd choice for a hotel) Also, my room only came with 2 towels and 2 hand towels- no face cloths and no extra towels. I left a note and tip for housekeeping and they were left for me. I did not complain about the cleanliness of my room, I was very disappointed but lived with it. Honestly, the overall condition of the bathroom was so bad, I am not sure it would have mattered.The pool was very nice, it was a great crowd, a beautiful pool and as long as you were there by 10:30 or so you could easily get a lounge chair in a good location but they did fill up. The beach had great soft sand and the water was gorgeous, but the pool was a better choice to sit and relax. The pool bar was nice as well.Overall, I would say if you are looking for a lively place to stay with a nice pool scene, good restaurants, and a great place to socialize and enjoy the music the El San Juan is a great spot. If you are looking for a more upscale room I would definitely choose the Ritz and just go over to the El San Juan at night. The Ritz appeared to have a quieter pool crowd and I saw children there- at El San Juan I think I only saw 2 children all weekend. However, I did not find the beach over at the Ritz as nice. It's definitely about what your priorities are when choosing between these two places.Puerto Rico was a great destination, Old San Juan was very quaint and clean and I wish I had more time to explore there. I would say Puerto Rico had a South Beach feel to it in many places, but without the attitude that you find in some places in South Beach! The El San Juan had it's good and bad points, I would consider staying there again- but would insist from the beginning on a clean room!

<Author>MrsTMatt
<Content>Could have been better... The El San Juan is a nice hotel. It definitely has a lot to offer but at the price it should include a few more perks for its guests. My husband and I stayed Sept. 19th - 23rd with about 10 other couples. My first impression of the hotel was it looked exactly like the website. The lobby is beautiful but it doesn't match the decor in the guest rooms at all which we all though was kind of odd. The guest rooms are a little to modern, Miami Vice-ish and left more to be desired. It is true the walls are PAPER THIN, we could hear the phone ringing in other rooms and you could hear all the conversations in the hallways. I'm very glad we weren't right next to the elevator because I'm sure you could hear every ding! The beds are definitely soft which is great if that's what you like but after a couple of days, my husbands back was hurting. The bathrooms weren't as small as the impression I got from other reviews, my husband and I were still able to shower at the same time, without too much of a hassle. I would suggest they grout the shower stall with a darker grout though. It was kind of dingy and dirty looking but of course that is going to happen with white tile and white grout. I can see why some guests found it unsanitary. The pleather furniture in the rooms was also uncomfortable. No one wants to sit on something that is going to either stick to them or that they feel like they're going to slide off of. We ate at 2 of the full service restaurants in the hotel, Yamato, a Benihana type restaurant had very good sushi and the prices were comparable with those in the States. The second restaurant we dined at was The Palm. The service here was exceptional. We had a private room for all the couples in our group and the waitstaff was wonderful. The food was excellent as well, the biggest problem was leftovers! The hotel does not provide a refrigerator for use. It is full with items from the mini bar and there is a $10 service fee if used for personal use! I found this to be ridiculous! My husband and I spent $150 for dinner and the leftovers went to complete waste because we didn't have anywhere to store it without incurring and additional fee. I understand them not wanting outside food and drink in the hotel but what about their guests that patronize their restaurants. We definitely kept this in mind when eating else where, making sure we didn't order more than we could eat in one seating. There was a bit of a tropical storm during our stay and the hotel lobby became a disaster area and probably more of a hazard than it appeared. Water literally poured from the ceiling in certain areas and dripped in several more. There was also some flooding on the 3rd floor about an inch or 2 on in the hallway of on wing and those guests had to be moved to other parts of the hotel. Seeing all the leaks really made us question the workmanship of the hotel itself. This is a tropical area and hurricanes and tropical storms are not unusual yet they didn't seem to be prepared structurally. It was definitely a good thing that it only rained for 2 days and that it didn't turn into a hurricane, I would hate to see what it might have looked like then. Overall the hotel was beautiful but still seems like a work in progress, there is definitely room for improvement. Most of the staff was courteous and efficient. If I were to go back to Puerto Rico, I would probably pick another hotel, the Intercontinental next door appeared to be very nice and I believe wasn't as expensive.

<Author>BostonLegal
<Content>Tons of Fun But Terrible Service First, the obvious: The El San Juan is THE place to be in Puerto Rico if you're looking to have fun and be social. If you stay at the hotel, you get into the club (Brava) for free (usually $30) and it's like a Bacardi commercial. I know that sounds cheesy, but it's true. Even if you don't want to be in the club, there is live music in the lobby, which is beautiful, and you can simply enjoy that for most of the night. Great crowd, too. Clearly, both locals and tourists from other hotels know that this is the place to come.The pool is great. Along with the rest of the hotel, it creates a Las Vegas-esque atmosphere. If you like the Palms, Hard Rock Hotel, or to a lesser extend Mandalay Bay, you'll love the El San Juan. It has swim up bars, cabanas, and all of those types of things. It's really fun to spend the day out there because you can bounce back and forth from the pool to the beach.What's missing from this hotel is service. There were a few pleasant staff members, but for the most part the hotel treated me and those with me like they were doing us a favor. In particular, the front desk, casino staff, and pool bar staff were not only rude, but moved at a snail's pace. I tried not to take it personally because most of the service industry in San Juan is not particularly friendly.Fortunately, most other Puerto Ricans are incredibly nice.In sum, this is really the best major hotel in the area. I've been to the Ritz, Marriott, e.a., and they are hotels that could be anywhere. At least here you feel like you're in Puerto Rico and it makes the poor service tolerable.

<Author>bandito912
<Content>Decent hotel, but needs a lot of work I attended a wedding at the El San Juan and read several dozen reviews from this site before I stayed there. The reviews are so varied I had no idea what to expect. Overall, I thought the hotel was mediocre, especially for the amount of money they charge. The positives: the pools are beautiful, beach access is fabulous, the lobby and bar are very stylish and trendy (especially with a weekend crowd), and the ballroom where the wedding was held was a perfect space for celebrating. The negatives: the room was designed entirely in white which made every speck of dirt visible (and there were many), the shower floor was filthy and mildewy, the mattresses on the poolside lounge chairs are left out in the rain and are covered in visible mildew spots and dirt (for some inexplicable reason the hotel only provides white slipcovers for some of the lounge chairs so the stains on the other chairs are visible for all the world to see), our reservation for a garden view room turned out to be a room on the third floor with only a two foot window near the ceiling, and the walls of the hotel are paper thin so you can expect to be woken up several times a night (if you are lucky enough to be able to fall asleep) because of noise in the hallway or a neighboring room. To echo a lot of the comments in other posts, even though it is the off season in Puerto Rico, we still had some difficulty finding available pool chairs. I didn't really think this was the end of the world, but the fact that people can reserve a chair for the entire day -- even though they never use it -- just by leaving a towel there is a bit ridiculous and it would be nice if the hotel had better control of that situation. I saw no sign of bedbugs, nor did I hear any of the other wedding guests voicing complaints about bedbugs, in spite of some of the other reviews. The island does have a lot of no-see-ums/sand mites and it wouldn't surprise me if the reviewers who complained about bedbugs had encountered some other insects out by the beach without realizing it.

The pool area is just beautiful. The hotel lobby is nice but too dark for my taste, but we didn't spend much time there anyway. We never had any problem getting extra bath towels as soon as we requested them. The renovated rooms are very bright and airy and I highly recommend asking for one of these rooms if you are going to stay here. I have no idea what all the bad reviews are about...we had no complaints whatsoever! If you book this hotel, you will not be sorry. I would stay here again in a heartbeat!

We would always hang out at the lobby and listen to the live music, which is great. Overall the hotel was ok, but the noise issue was a huge deal for us as we were looking for a relaxing, romantic vacation. If you are looking for a relaxing, quiet vacation, with really good service this might not be the best hotel.

<Author>lromansky
<Content>Awesome, Beautiful Hotel made for a Great Vacation! Just got back from an amazing stay at the El San Juan Hotel  Casino for 5 nights. First of all, the place is amazing. I'm a pretty snobby traveler and have high standards for quality of hotels, bars and restaurants. I am not understanding what these people are thinking who can't give this hotel good remarks! I honestly have nothing bad to say about the place!We stayed Tuesday, July 1st - Sunday, July 6th. We stayed in an un-remodeled Garden Lanai room, on the ground floor of the building (room 165). These rooms haven't been remodeled because in my opinion, they simply do not need it yet. Yes, it's not as modern as the highrise building where most of the hotel rooms are located, but these have a more rustic/classy appeal than the newly remodeled rooms (which I don't think really go with the style of the resort anyway). Our bed was comfortable, the tiles on the floor were nice, the furniture was very nice, the bathroom was big with modern fixtures and granite countertops, as was the large single shower and stand-alone soaking tub. The decor was very tasteful and elegant. We also had a wet bar, with dark wood and granite countertops. The best part was that with the lanai room, we had a huge patio that stepped out in to the garden and a hot-tub, which we never even requested upon check-in!The resort itself is gorgeous. There are 3 pools and 3 hot-tubs. Plenty of places to lay down with comfortable padded lounge chairs and beds. Though I will say that they are hard to get on the weekends so get up early to reserve one.We like the beach better than the pool so we spent most of our days out there. The hotel has plenty of beach loungers and umbrellas to use. The ocean was clear blue and very warm. They have all kinds of water sports (wave runners, boats, parasailing, etc.) to do there but of course you have to pay for that. We paid $70 for a waverunner for a half hour which we thought was a pretty good pirce.We dined at 4 of the many hotel restaurants. We ate lunch a few times at the beach club by the pool. It was very good food, though a little pricey for lunch but as expected for such a nice upscale resort. If you want cheaper food there are tons of restaurants down the street in Isla Verde, all within a few blocks. We also ate at the Pizza Restaurant located in the galleria area, which was very good. One evening we dined at Yamato, which was excellent, and another night at Koco, which was even better - the food here was absolutely delicious.At night the El San Juan Casino comes alive - there are 4 bars in the lobby and by 10 PM the place is jam packed. For anyone who likes a hip upscale scene, this is the place to be especially on weekends. Each of the 3 main bars were filled with people (mostly in their 20's to 40's) and there was always live salsa music and people will dance. Then later in the evening they open up another area behind where the salsa band plays which becomes another bar, seperate from the others with live bands  music. Then after 11 there is an area where they play modern - top 40, pop, hip hop, etc.During our stay we took walks down the road in Isla Verde where the El San Juan was located and checked out all of the hotels and even ate at a few local restaurants. Here is my opinion on the other hotels on the road:1. Ritz Carlton - very nice....but blah with a capital B. It almost felt like a retirement home. So quiet, so stiff... Don't get me wrong, ti's very nice, but it has no atmosphere like some of the other Ritz Carltons I've stayed at. The pool is nice, but again - boring. And, the lounge chairs there aren't nearly as nice as at El San Juan. Everyone at the Ritz seemed to be aged 50+. This Ritz does not compare to South Beach Ritz Carlton, which has a hip vibe, or the one in Georgetown, DC which also is a very good scene. This one really is boring. My husband and I were SO GLAD we didn't choose the Ritz b/c it was between ESJ and the Ritz.2. Intercontinental - again very nice... I give this a better score than the Ritz, but again - very boring as well. NO atmosphere, just a very nice hotel. We did eat at their beach club restaurant one afternoon and it was good with an island/casual feel, but other than that as far as the hotel and pool area is concerned...boring boring boring. 3. Water Club - We liked this hotel... it's more of a very small boutique hotel, which is very different from ESJ, RItz or Intercontinental. Their pool is on the rooftop and is super teeny tiny. The lobby is also tiny as is the restaurant, Tangerine (which we ate at one night and was awesome). But the hotel is very cool so if you like small boutiquey hotels, this is a good choice. They also have a club up top called Wet and we went to a party there on Thursday night. Actually the party was located on 3 floors of the hotel, they had 80's on the ground level, 90's on the 2nd floor and then modern music on the rooftop where we were. The views are amazing and it felt like a South Beach Miami scene there.One night we went to Old San Juan, which is about a 10 minute taxi from Isla Verde and costs roughly $20 each way. We dined at Aquavia (sp?) and it was awesome. OSJ is beautiful, a definite must see if you head to Puerto Rico.The other nights (besides the Water Club evening and the OSJ evening) we just hung out at our hotel, mostly in the various lobby bars, each one has it's own unique kind of scene. Lots of interesting people to watch.... it was just so fun and happening. Oh and we gambled a little bit. Never even had a problem getting on a blackjack table at night!The talks of bedbugs, rude service, bad hotel rooms, etc. is ridiculous. My only guess is that these people who say these things is that perhaps they are elderly and unable to deal with a fun scene and think outside bug bites are bed bugs or something? There are sand fleas on the beach (which the hotel warns of and provides OFF for free) and the hotel warns you that if you go to the beach in the early AM or late PM you should use the OFF provided. We never went out on the beach late but laid out on the beach every day from 10 AM - 3 PM and never got bitten once .Bottom line I give my highest recommendations for the El San Juan Hotel  Casino and would recommend it to anyone interested in going. And Puerto Rico is gorgeous - a must see.

<Author>dreamvac
<Content>Stay next door at the Intercontinental and visit the El San Juan I just returned from a week stay at the ESJ. This was my 3d visit to San Juan. Previously I had stayed at the Intercontinental next door and the Marriott in Condado. Each visit I booked through hotwire. The first 2 visits were using the blind hotel purchase whereby you are told the hotel class and ammenities but not the hotel. This stay was purchase through the hotwire packages where we were told the name of the hotel and could choose our flight. All reservations through Hotwire were fine.I chose the El San Juan because it was a little less expensive than the Intercontinental. I wanted to stay in the Isla Verde section of San Juan over Condado and did not want to risk using the blind Priceline and Hotwire options since I could have ended up in Condado.I prefer Isla Verde over Condado because the water in Isla Verde is calmer than in Condado where the surf can be very rough.Overall, if I return I would stay at the Intercontinental next door to the El San Juan and just visit the El San Juan. The Intercontinental was just a couple of hundred more for the week and would have been worth it. Tripadvisor has the El San Juan rated as a 5 . It is NOT A FIVE STAR RESORT!!We arrived by taxi from the airport. No doorman or bellman greeted us to assist with the bags and open the door. The entrance pours into the breathtaking lobby bar with its paneled walls and marble. It is a beautiful lobby. We were promptly checked in and given a remodeled room in the main building. The room looked like the pictures showing the orange drapes. It is ultra modern and trendy. There is no balcony and the room overlooked a roof. When I checked in I asked about a room with a better view and was told the check the next day. Note that most of the rooms do not have an ocean view.The room was clean, but overall cleanliness at the resort ranges from poor to average. As mentioned by others, the pools do not appear to be sparkling clean. Plumbing at the pool bathroom was poor and my husband walked into a flithy men's room with feces flooding the floor. The lady's room by the pool had flushing problems as well. Breakfast trays were allowed to lay out for 12 hours without being picked up. This was a regular occurrence.Service overall ranges from poor to below average. We spent most of our days around the pool and beach. The pool bartenders and waitresses were terrible. We were basically ignored pretty much the whole time unless we really had to push for their attention. The drinks and food are expensive, which is ok if the service and quality are there, but in light of the lack of service, we ended up bringing our own cooler and ate lunch away from the resort. One lazy waitress then proceeded to scold us about the cooler and told us not to bring one to the pool. Meanwhile others had their coolers as well. Next door at the Intercontinental when we stayed the pool service was outstanding and caring. The ESJ would have earned more money from us around the pool if they took care of us.The pool and beach are lovely, but I think the grounds at the Intercontinental are better.The next day we were moved to a garden lanai room in one of the low rise buildings. The room was not updated, but was in ok condition furnished in traditional furniture. It was certainly not luxurious or a 5 star room. There was a patio with a very old hot tub.The benefit of the ESJ is the entertainment. Almost evernight there is live music in the lobby. We particularly enjoyed the latin jazz group on Sunday Night, Charlie Suplveda. He is an excellent trumpet player and polished professional musician. However the next night the flamenco guitars were not on time and then was like canned elevator music.We do not gamble, but suggest that the casino be upgraded to meet the Ritz Carlton's casino which had sports betting as well as other gambling options.We mostly ate away from the hotel. There are many excellent local and afforable restaurants in walking distance. For lunch on the beach we really like Cafe Mediterranian at the Intercontinental where we ate 3 days for lunch and the excellent waitress there remembered us and seemed to appreciate us. It is not inexpensive, but the view is breathtaking. The cubano is one of the best we have enjoyed and there is a good selection of salads and other sandwiches.Other favorites are Lupis right next door, a sports bar with mexican food, Mi Casita, a local restuarant that serves breakfast, lunch and dinner with delicious local dishes at very low prices and great service, and Metropole, a great local restaurant where the roast pork was unbelievable.We had a great time in San Juan and the issues did not ruin our trip, but I would look for one of the other resorts for better service and cleanliness. I really feel that we didn't really matter at the ESJ. They really need to work on that.

<Author>twopenguins
<Content>Noisy Nights, Nice Pools and Good Food My husband and I just came back from staying here for 5 nights and were in a Grande Vista room on the 9th floor, half-way down the hall from the elevators. The little bathroom tiles had mold in the grout lines and it was very unpleasant to shower. The internet was sketchy at best and very slow. There was noise all night from the time we went to sleep until the next morning (we were told we had a 'quiet room'). People were slamming doors, talking and yelling in the halls. I think the problem is that the doors are not thick and there are spaces all around them. Also the lack of carpeting inside the rooms probably magnifies the noise. We resorted to putting a damp towel at the base of the door to try to muffle SOME of the noise, but it didn't help very much. The noise from the airport didn't bother us at all. It was hardly noticeable unless you were outside and then it was only a mild, thunder-like rumble. Temperature-wise, we set the thermostat in our room to 65 Deg. (the lowest it would go) yet still managed to sweat all night long. The AC probably needs to be charged. The food was expensive but good. I would recommend the rooftop Mexican resturant for a good deal and good food. Outside of the resort, we had a difficult time locating places to eat that were clean, and air conditioned and after hunting around for two days, we decided not to leave except for the excursions we had planned. Some things that we did like were the magnificent pools and hot tubs. They were very clean the entire time we were there. We never had trouble getting a lounge or spot to relax. We also loved how comfortable the beds were... too bad we didn't get to sleep soundly in them.We came here to SCUBA dive and booked with an awesome and professional company named Sea Ventures Dive Centers. For a $25.00 per person fee, a van would come and pick us up, take us to the marina (about an hour's drive) and drop us off back at our hotel afterwards. The people running this company are courteous and the dives and rental gear are not overpriced like others we looked into. If you are doing more than a one-day dive, you can get a 10% discount as a repeat customer for the second dive. We had an awesome time with awesome dive masters who pointed out all sorts of wildlife and who took care of all the gear from start to finish. We didn't have to lift a finger. There were sodas and waters and snacks on the boat between dives and we were lucky to have perfect weather.Also... in response to the people complaining about bed bugs.... there are little gnats on the beach and around the resort sometimes. They bite up your legs and arms and you get a red bump. They are pretty good about making sure the resort grounds are sprayed, but venturing onto the beach is a different story. I am sure there were no bed bugs in our room or any bugs of any type.

<Author>MRDJ422
<Content>Some good, some bad, but definitely overpriced. Just came off a 6 day, 5 night stay at El San Juan, traveling with a bunch of friends in their mid-twenties. This is definitely a party hotel, and the lobby gives that away right off the bat with an assortment of very impressive bar areas and restaurants. The lobby is pretty calm during the day, but at night its very exciting if you want to party. The pool area is also very nice, with three different pools, swim-up bar, a few nice hot tubs and alot of comfortable seats to lounge in. Pool area was a big plus for me.Now the bad stuff...My room was kept very nice and clean, but we saw a bunch of our friends' room, and one room had a problem with ants in the bathroom, another room had really gross mold and mildew in the showers, and one of our friends in another floor had such noise problems that they could barely sleep any of the nights. I personally did not have any of these problems, but we saw three rooms that did, so I guess its a bit of the luck of the draw there.The hotel staff, especially at the front desk, was generally pretty rude and sometimes even outright mean. One concierge outright lied to us when we asked about the means of transportation to get to the El Yunque rainforest, and another was extremely condescending when asking about restaurants that had vegetarian options (PR is not very big on that FYI). There were a couple nice and patient front desk workers, but overall, the attitude was still poor. Overall, my experience was positive, but you have to be willing to overpay for the value, and you may get a really loud floor or a poor room. It is a great place for 20-30 year olds that want to party.

<Author>motherbored
<Content>A great place to party and meet a variety of cultures This is a wonderful, lively hotel with a fabulous pool and beach area; excellent, attentive staff; and great nightlife. The restaurant selections are numerous with outstanding food and great service. The rooms are spacious and clean. This is not a good hotel for sleeping; and obviously the hotel must know this because instead of providing chocolates during turn-down service, the hotel staff places earplugs at your bedside (no kidding, really). I have never been in a hotel that provided earplugs. Our room was near the elevator and ice machine (rooms X31, X33, X35)--people got off the elevator at all hours and continued their conversations and frivolity in the hallway. It got quiet at around 5 AM. You'll need to catnap at the pool and beach.The nightlife is electric and fun. Each night, the eclectically-adorned lobby area is filled with wildly-attired guests and visitors from a variety of cultures and age groups. The younger-hip crowd migrates to Bravo, the on-site, very popular club. The older crowd dances to the live Latin bands in the lobby with incredible flare and charisma--it's a blast just watching them. This is a fantastic hotel for a reunion of friends, bachelor party, sorority/fraternity reunion, young people, families with older teens, twenty and thirty somethings. I know the hotel has a variety of rooms, and I believe honeymooners can have privacy and a great time, as well. The casino is like most hotel casinos--nothing remarkable.We loved the pool area--the landscaping, waterfalls, private areas are just magnificent. The staff is great about coming around and serving you yummy drinks and treats, fixing your umbrella, dispensing towels, etc.Tip: Move your shower dial no more than a half an inch to the right to turn on the water and set the temperature control. Any further movement to the right will result in a VERY hot shower.

<Author>boog-a-boo71

All really had a great time. We were worried after reading all the reviews...bed bugs, no chairs, unfriendly staff, noise, lousy rooms, lousy showers, blah, blah, blah,... Well, there aren't any bed bugs. There are mosquitos and sand gnats on the island (isn't that a surprise), bring some OFF, you'll be fine. Of coarse there are chairs, there are TWO pools  a Beach (plus hammocks). I really doubt any hotel you go to will have a chair per guest at the hotel, that is an unrealistic request! And again, 20 of us went and somehow each of us had a chair everyday! The staff was as friendly as any other place we have travelled to. I guess it would depend on how friendly you are with them. They gave suggestions on nightlife, restaurants, things to see, things to do, were polite  respectful. My suggestion is don't be demanding and rude and RELAX... your on vacation. I do want to compliment specifically Yvonne Ramos  Miguel at the front desk. They were above  beyond when it came to hospitality and helping our group out. Next time, if you have any issues, I suggest you look for these two employees. Thank-you both! We stayed in the garden-lanai rooms ( had an opportunity to upgrade, decided not to) . The rooms were more than spacious, had our own balcony, walk-in closet, sitting area(for make-up girls) double sinks, king bed  sitting area...oh yes, 2 in our group got hot tubs on their balcony. One room did have a problem with a safe, but we called security ,they came, it was fixed! As far as the noise goes...people go here for a vacation, to enjoy themselves, to relax, to let loose, to laugh out loud and not worry about the real world for awhile. When your going out ,you do want a crowd, whether it's in the lobby, in the casino, in the club, at the pool,or at the restaurants. This actually means the place is worth going to  makes the atmosphere more fun  the time more enjoyable. It was never so crowed you could not get into somewhere or had such a long wait you would want to leave. HINT: No crowd...best bet...not good! If you want no crowd, no wait, someone waiting on you hand  foot, no noise...I suggest you rent a house  a pritvate chef somewhere off the beaten path. I guess to sum it up, I would reccomend this hotel  would myself go back in a heartbeat. A vacation is really what you make of it and the El San Juan is a great backdrop...Nice rooms, beautifuls pools (forgot to mention pool chairs AMAZING!) ( I would though, suggest either a live band or a dj at the pools, the generic recorded music was more annoying than enjoyable) friendly  efficient staff, a very fun atmosphere in lobby, casino, and we all had a really great time at Club Brava. All in all good hotel/good vacation! P.S. Food is expensive, but your eating in the hotel, it's like that everywhere! It's not an all-inclusive! For breakfast  great cubans try Edith's next door. Lupi's is good for lunch  dinner. There is also Mi Casitas  Metropol, all walking distance. Or hop in a cab to Old San Juan, there you have more than enough options for dining  things to do day or night! Have fun!

<Author>RobSport
<Content>Its a Mixed Bag... I read every review on this hotel and still went ahead and booked this through Priceline because of its 4 stars.Let me start with the positive first..The hotel is very beautiful and has a magnificent lobby area. The pool area is to die for and the beach access was wonderful. Unlike other reviews, I had no issues finding a pool chair and the pool was very clean.The rooms were quite elegant and extremely clean, although the shower temperature water was extremely hot and couldn't get it to cool down my entire stay. I would suggest that you don't get a room near an elevator. I was next to the elevator and could hear the hotel's party crowd very late each evening. There is an all night club in this hotel and the lobby bar is also packed until the middle of the night..Then you hear everyone stumlinig to their rooms at 4 and 5am which was annyoing.Also because of the proximity to the airport, you constantly hear planes taking off and landing...Once I got into a deep sleep, it didn't wake me, but its definitely constant if you are in your roomCasino was ok...Most of the black jack dealers don't like to talk to you (especially if you speak English). They prefer to have personal conversatioins with the local spanish speaking customers..It surprises me that they don't socialize more with everyone as this is how they make their tips. Although, Ruben was the exception to the rule. He was outstanding!!My final issue is that the hotel charges you a one time Resort Fee of 17.50 which they don't tell you about at check in, but when you check out, they tell you that you signed for it when you checked in, but of course they don't point this out to you. When I complained about it, I was told that there was nothing they can do. I don't understand why a resort that charges so much money has to add this charge..Isn't that what you are already paying for?The Isla Verde area has some great hotels (Ritz Carlton, Intercontinental, Embassy Suites, etc..) but other than that its a bunch of chain restaurants with long lines. If this is your first trip, I would definitely recommend staying either in Old San Juan or on the Condado (if you like the beach). The Condado has some great hotels, great shopping and great restaurants and you can walk everywhere...There is much more culture in Old San Juan and Condado than in Isla Verde.

<Author>jone7768
<Content>Loved the Hotel We just returned from a 4 day vacation at the El San Juan Hotel and Casino. Having read the various reviews, I was somewhat nervous about the trip going into it. We had a great time and overall I would recommend this hotel. However, it may not be for everyone as there are things about the hotel that may be a turn off for some and not for others.The hotel lobby and outdoor decor is stunning. We visited rooms in both the main tower and the Garden Lanai and both types of rooms were nice. They rooms in the tower are slightly smaller and have been decorated in a modern look. The rooms in the Garden Lanai have a more traditional look. For us personally, we greatly preferred the Garden Lanai rooms and would have probably been disappointed had we had to stay in the tower. The hotel is definitely one for partiers. They have a techno club and a club that plays Latin music. The partying goes to 4:00 am. If you stay in the Tower, I understand that the partying can be disturbing. I can't imagine how the people in the rooms directly above the clubs sleep.The Garden Lanai rooms are away from the main tower, in a seperate building on the other side of the pool. It was quiet on that side of the hotel. The rooms were much larger and more spacious. Our rooms were clean and we didn't experience any of the issues that we read from other travelers with the cleanliness of the room.The hotel prices on food are pricey and that did initially put me off. To give you an idea, on day one we ordered room service for breakfast. A coffee, OJ, bagel and a single serving of cereal cost $35. However, we soon founds ways to cope. There is a super market a block up the street and we brought back food and stored it in the frig in our room. There are several restaurants and fast food places within a short walking distance of the hotel. There is a Starbucks on site and they do serve croissant sandwiches and pastries at the normal Starbucks prices. The other best deal on the resort for kids is the pizza. You can't take it out to the pool but you can carry it out to the beach. Definetely eat at the Texas restaurant that's on the 10th floor. They have a mechanical bull and it's a blast watching people try to ride it. The food was great and since it's on the top floor, there is a great view. Food servings at all the restaurants we ate at were huge. You may want to split meals. We threw away so much food when we ate out. If you go anywhere that has local cuisine try the Mofongo (delicious Puerto Rican dish). If you like strong coffee, definetely try the Puerto Rican coffee at the hotel. I loved it.The hotel has several pools and hot tubs. The one closest to the beach does fill up. We never were able to get chairs over there as we weren't the kind to get up early and hold our spot. Yes, people do leave their towels and there is plenty of empty seats with no people in them but you can't use them because they've got towels on them. We didn't press the issue because we had no trouble finding seats by the other pool and on the beach. The pool chairs are great. They have thick cushions on them and they are so comfortable you can easily fall asleep.I had the absolute best massage ever at the spa. Don't leave without getting one.If you like to dance, definetly go down and check out the clubs. The techno club was definetely for a younger crowd. The music was a little too loud for our taste and the floor too packed though the younger crowd seemed to love it. We loved the Latin music club and had a great time watching some of the dancers and trying it out for ourselves.The beach was lovely. Be forewarned that there is seaweed in it and it washes up to shore. They periodically clean the seaweed off the beach and the seaweed stays near the shore so you just need to go out a little ways in the ocean to get clear water. The water is shallow and doesn't drop off which is great for kids. During our stay, the water was calm and very nice. However since you are on the Atlantic side, if there are storms, the water can get rough. We didn't have it during this trip but have had it during others.My two complaints were that the safe in the room did not work. They said they've lost the key to get into them for emergencies and weren't allowing people to use them. You can store your belongings in the lobby safe but I found that incovenient. The second is that we went to the pools in the late afternoon/early evening on our first day in. They were dirty and there was some disgusting scum floating in one of the hot tubs. We didn't experience this problem any other time and I think during the busy hours, they do a good job of keeping the pools and hot tubs clean. I was extremely put out by the dirt in the pool and thought that for a hotel of that quality, they ought to keep the cleanliness up to par even if it's past the busy hour.Overall we loved it and would recommend it. Just be aware of the above and make sure it's the place for you. I've also stayed at the Marriott Stellaris and would recommend it as well.I absolutely love Puerto Rico. It's my third time there and I can't wait to go again.

No one was rude to us when they were helping us, however.You definitely need to get out early and get your lounge chairs. They do fill up quickly and I will agree that there may not be enough in comparison to how many people the hotel is able to accomodate. There were always chairs available on the beach, which we had to default to twice. Again, you're sitting on a white sand beach on a tropical island as opposed to poolside...it's a rough life. We still went in the pool even though our chairs were on the beach and vice versa on the days we had poolside chairs.Food at the hotel is expensive for sure, but not unexpected since most resorts are sort of like that. Pretty much New York prices on things, which is what I am used to. We did eat lunch there a few times. We started eating outside of the hotel for breakfast and dinner. If you walk towards the Ritz on the main road there is a great Puerto Rican restaurant, the food and service were great and it had a good atmosphere. We also went into Old San Juan at night for dinner, there are a lot of great places. Cab ride was about 15 - 20 dollars. I like to venture out of the hotel for things, so I didn't need to eat at the hotel every day for every meal. I don't think the El San Juan should be compared to the Ritz, that is a different class of hotel. You get what you pay for. I thought the hotel was hip, the bars were cool. The crowd was good for us singles, not a huge amount of families with small children. It was a great getaway in a beautiful place. When you travel you have to be able to roll with the punches and it seemed like some of the past reviews were a bit picky about minor things. (We arrived at 11:00am. ) We requested a TowerRoom and were in the room within 10 minutes. Unfortunately, I did not like the room because it was too futuristic and cold looking and it didn't have a balcony. This was the only real dislike I had and it was somewhat subjective on my part. I went downstairs and spoke to Yvonne Ramos. She is the assistant desk manager. I cannot say enough about this lovely woman. The El San Juan is very lucky to have some one at the front desk with her people skills. ( If you encounter ANY problems while you are there, ask for her!) When I expressed my disappointment with the lack of a balcony, she said she would give us another room in the garden lanai area. She also told me that these rooms were not really updatedso I should know that . However, if we would leave our cell phone number she would call us when someone checked out so that we could see if we liked that room better. She went on to say that she only wanted to make us happy with our stay at the hotel and anything she could do to help us, she would. Can't ask for more than that! We also were allowed to stay and use the room we were first assigned until another became available. We also went at a very busy time. April 18- 26. The lanai room was perfect for us even though it was older and we enjoyed hearing the couqui frogs at night. The casino and lobby areas were always busy and there always seemed to be something going on. (Live music, bars, some people dancing, HOT club, restaurants etc.) The beach was beautiful and again it was clean and well maintained. There are a limited number of umbrella's at $10/day so if you want to stay on the beach for the day and you need shade, you might want to get one. However, you can also get a chair under one of the plam trees and not have the umbrella. We were in love with the lounges by the pool with the billowy curtains on them. I will say that on a busy time, you need to get up at 6:45 am to get one. The towel hut opens at 7am and you have to be there to put your towels on them. This being said, Wes is the pool manager. He will find you chairs etc. even if there does not seem to be any. If you don't use your lounges and leave towels on them to reserve them, they will be taken offafter a half hour if the hotel is busy. I loved being up early as the staff is out cleaning at 6am and the hotel is so pretty in the morning. You can get your coffee at Starbuck's and walk the beach. A word about Starbuck's.. there are two. Go to the one in the Galeria(right around the corner from the one in the lobby). There is usually not a wait at this one.  You can walk right out the front door.. to the right there are Wendy's, Burger King and some local food places. Nice if you want something less formal ( and expensive) than the hotel. Also, right next door is the Inter-Continental. We played at their casino but I would NOT recommend this hotel over the El San Juan. It is older and smelled musty. Some of the slot machines in the casino still used coins!!! However, half of the hotel rooms do have the ocean view as they face the ocean. On the left side of the hotel is Lupi's a fun bar for a beer, nacho';s etc. Also, there is a Denny's ( we went there for breakfast one morning) and the Ritz. The Rtiz has a great casino that serves soup and sandwiches right on the casino floor! We had the best meal while we were in Puerto Rico at the Ritz at the Il Forno restaurant. (Italian) This meal was so delicious,the restaurant was very romantic and was the highlight of the food portion of our trip. Make reservations and eat there, you will not be disappointed. All in all, I think that the El San Juan has been given a very bad and undeserved poor review. Our experience was nothing but wonderful I will go back again and hopefully stay in the oceanfront lanais. ( the newest and most expensive!). Enjoy your trip and don't let bad reviews spoil the anticipation of your vacation.

<Author>CruisinFlorida
<Content>El San What? Recently my family and I had occasion to visit the El San Juan before embarking on a cruise to the Southern Caribbean. After hearing rave reviews from others who had either stayed at the resort or visited the casino, we decided to give it a try. Unfortunately, the reviews were not well founded. Upon arriving at the hotel around 2:00 in the afternoon and waiting on line at a reception area that at all times was inadequately manned, we met with a reception clerk who should be greeting customers in a parking garage cashier's office, not the front desk of a hotel. We were thereafter told that check in time was 4 pm and that our room was not ready. I found it somewhat hard to believe that a hotel of this size would not have any rooms that were cleaned by such time, but unfortuntely this clerk was not about to go out of her way to help us out. In fact, upon arrival at the desk, she made us stand there for several minutes while she attended to other affairs without even acknowledging our presence. Other visits to the front desk were oftentimes met with the same greeting. Nevertheless, after an hour or so, we were finally told that a room was available and that it was an upgrade from what we had reserved. We were then given the key to a room which I would not have allowed my dog to stay in. First, the room was not an upgrade as I recalled that rooms in the building at issue were less expensive than the room we had reserved. Second the room was dark, damp and dank. Certainly not the accomodation one would expect at a major resort hotel. After promptly returning to the front desk to advise them of our concerns and of course waiting quite some time to speak with another clerk, we were given a room in the tower which is what we had reserved in the first place. While more open and brighter, this room was nothing to write home about. We found at least one towel in the bath room dirty and the floor was filfthy with hairs and other materials everywhere. Additionally, the bathroom was tiny and very dark. After quickly changing, we rushed to the beach where we found various personnel clearing chairs. While we searched for some chairs for ourselves not one person approached us to assist. The lobby is somewhat eclectic and the casino staff played their games at a snail's pace. We had dinner at the Palm restaurant located in the lobby. While dinner was good, we certainly did not need to travel to Puerto Rico to eat there since we have a Palm restaurant close to where we live. All in all, there must be better choices in San Juan.

<Author>swingchickie
<Content>Great experience at the El San Juan Just had to add my own review of the El San Juan now that my BF and I are back from spending a week there last week... We read so many negative reviews on here, we were a little worried about our vacation, but we had a great time. Here's my scoop:Rooms: we stayed in the main tower, and the rooms are just as gorgeous as on their website. Clean, modern, spacious. We had no issues with water splashing out of the shower, we just made sure the curtain was pulled in all the way. The walls are rather thin, and for some reason people tend to slam their doors (the doors don't automatically slam shut), so if you're a light sleeper you should be aware of that. We thought it was hysterical that the hotel actually provides earplugs in a little El San Juan case, just in case you need them.Restaurants: I can't say this strongly enough -- Koco (the modern Caribbean restaurant) is PHENOMENAL. The best meal of our vacation, so good we went back for the final night of our trip. First time we shared all the appetizers as our meal, second time we had a couple of apps and then got entrees. Everything we ate there was oh my god, TRY this! good, and the service was great as well. The Italian restaurant was nice, the staff is actually from Italy and very service-oriented. The pizza in the pizza place was nummy (they make their crust with garlic in it) and the lunch menu at the pool, while limited and expensive, was pretty decent. The sushi restaurant was a bit overrated, we've had better sushi here in Philadelphia. (We saw some people getting sushi and pizza delivered to them at the pool, not a bad idea if you don't want to order off the pool menu.)Pool and beach: the pools are very nice, the area is beautifully landscaped and the piped-in latin ambient lounge music makes the whole scene very relaxing and hip. we happened to be at the hotel on a slower week, so we had no issues with getting a lounge chair... as a matter of fact, we switched to different areas of the pool as the day went on, to make sure we had an umbrella that was shading us well (that sun is strong!). [If you can afford it, splurge on one of the cabanas by the pool with the swim-up bar -- for $800 you get a fridge full of water and juices, a massive fruit tray with mangoes and strawberries, a full-sized pitcher of sangria (which lasted us all day, it was so big), a flat-screen TV, a speaker dock for your iPod, extra towels, and attentive service for food and other bar drinks (food and other drinks aren't part of the charge). Not to mention shade when you need to go inside, and 4 lounge chairs reserved for you right there.] We arrived on a very busy Sunday, but were still able to find 2 lounge chairs and an umbrella by just asking one of the pool stewards and tipping him a few dollars. Drink service around the pool was slow, so we just walked up to the bar and ordered our drinks there. No biggie. The beach is really nice, you can rent an umbrella for $10... and you will definitely get a few sand flea bites, that just comes with the territory in Puerto Rico. Staff: we found the staff to be very friendly and helpful no matter where we went. Everyone on staff said hi to us as we passed them on the property. We mentioned one day that the guests staying next to us the night before had been rather loud, and the front desk clerk was upset that we hadn't mentioned it to them because they would have taken care of it for us. The bartenders at each pool are super-nice, especially at the swim-up bar. Service in every restaurant was very attentive. Got excellent massages in the rooftop spa, and when I was accidentally charged the wrong massage rate, they immediately fixed it on my bill with no complaint. (If you book a massage online before your stay, double-check rates with them because some of the prices on there are wrong.)Other things to note: there is no smoking on the property, except for on the beach or in a room off of the hotel entrance (this is a Puerto Rico law, no smoking in public, not even by the pool). There is a dress code in the evenings, they like to maintain a nice atmosphere in the lobby since it's part bar/nightclub then. People also like to look nice by the pool, regardless of shape or size... the couple of Budweiser shirts, or t-shirts with sayings on them, that we saw looked completely out of place.All in all, we had a great time. We went into our vacation with the intent of just relaxing and going with the flow, and I think that made our stay as nice as it was... we weren't in a rush for our food or drinks by the pool, we woke up early enough to grab breakfast and lounge chairs by the pool, and didn't need everyone checking with us constantly to see if we needed anything. We were nice to the staff, and we tipped well, so they were good to us in return. If, for your vacation, you want to wake up at 11am and still have plenty of lounge chairs to choose from, no lines at the bar, and people jumping to fill your every need, then going to one of the most popular resorts in the Caribbean during the high season probably isn't a good idea. (My BF and I saw a number of people being rude to the staff throughout our stay, and we were horrified.) We'd certainly stay there again.

<Author>Beantowntrekker
<Content>Manage your expections... We stayed at the ESJ for three nights at the end of March. I was reading the reviews here and got frightened--either they are glowing or awful and I was afraid to take the chance. We couldn't get into our alternate choice hotel and had to stay here. We requested the newly renovated tower upon our arrival and were told that we could have a room there, but that the room wasn't ready yet. That was fine with us, but at around 6pm we wanted to check in after hanging out at the pool, I went in to check and see if our room was ready. It wasn't, however the manager upgraded us to a suite on the third floor. It was essentially two rooms combined. It was clean and no bed bugs in sight. We really cannot complain--though I was afraid at first that we weren't in the tower. My overall comments about the ESJ. I think that this property was let go a few years ago and they are now trying to bring it back up to it's former glory--this is going to take some time. I believe in a couple of years, it will be what people expect. Service and cleanliness are adequate, but keep in mind, this is not a Disney World location. Yes, the pool deck should be hosed off every day, but it's not. The oceanside lounges need to be replaced, the hallways in the hotel itself need to be vacuumed more consistently than they are, the beach area could be raked from debris/cigarette butts, etc. It's kind of like a grande dame that needs a face lift.That said, the hotel lobby with the four bars, casino and restaurants provide a great place to find a seat at night and people watch. It's definitely a 'scene' and I'm glad that we stayed there. Note that there really is no breakfast place there--a Starbucks kiosk and a larger storefront around the back are there--but no real sit-down, reasonable place for breakfast--that would be on my wish list for this place. The hotel does provide a restaurant (Aquos I think is the name) that serves breakfast--but oatmeal is $14, so clearly they aren't relying, or don't want, a breakfast crowd. We stayed at three hotels during our week-long stay in PR, and each one was very different--we are glad that we stayed here.(My other reviews will appear for the Copamarina and the Wyndham Rio Mar.)

<Author>eurovoyageur
<Content>1 week at the El San Juan - LOVED IT! I just returned from a fabulous 1 week holiday in Puerto Rico. I'll admit I was a little apprehensive about the ESJ based on travelers reviews I had read but this hotel exceeded my expectations. I stayed in the Tower (5th floor), in a standard room with two beds and it was immaculately clean, quite spacious and quiet. Here are some of the great features....1) Perfect location (Isla Verde) for a vacation - just far enough from city to be able to relax and 10 minutes by car to Condado/Old San Juan. ESJ is right on the beach.2) Great beach, ocean is lovely and warm, no worries about undertow or overly large waves. 3) Beautiful grounds with palm trees, orchids, banyon trees, just breathtaking.4) Lots of action in the lobby (music, dancing etc) especially on weekends. Whether you participate or not (I didn't) I liked the Latin spirit of this place and the feeling you were actually in San Juan. This hotel is a true original.5) Lovely staff, especially when you take the time to smile and say hello. The Puerto Ricans are wonderful and warm people- make the effort to get to know a few.Here is a response to some of the criticisms:1) There are NO bedbugs. There are what they call no see 'ums on the beach, especially early or late in the day. Make sure you get a chair when on the beach (don't sit on a towel on the beach) and if you are the kind of person who tends to get bitten (ie: by mosquitos) bring repellent. I got a few bites, my friend was only bitten once. A small price to pay :)2) Yes, the hotel is older and no, maybe it's not really a business hotel. But I saw business people in the lobby each morning accessing the internet with their computers, Starbucks coffee in hand. Clearly they managed and they looked pretty content in doing so.3) On only one day in seven, there was a lot of seaweed near the shore - not sure why (wind, tides??) but it was gone the next day.4) Yes, things might get done a little more slowly at ESJ....much like the rest of San Juan and probably Puerto Rico in general. But things do get done. I quite liked the pace and came home completely relaxed. Take it easy, it's good for you.If you want a hotel just like the ones in any large U.S. City maybe this isn't the one for you. But if you're willing to scratch the surface and have a real cultural experience - I highly recommend the El San Juan. I'll go back.

<Author>prettyritz
<Content>Beware Ritz lovers - don't stay here After staying at the Ritz here in June 07 we wer eager to come back to Puerto Rico so when my husband received info on a conference here we leaped at the opportunity. We debated on staying at the Ritz again vs the El San Juan where the conference was being held. The room rate was around $400 per night more for Ritz concierge level so we made what turned out to be a poor decision based solely on $$$ and booked at the El San Juan (they had a package to receive a 5th night free). A friend said he stayed there in the past and it was fine. If I had followed my usual routine and readTrip Advisor reviews we would have made a different decision and booked at the Ritz - foolish me. We chose a La Vista tower room because they were renovated. While there we visited a non-renovated garden lanai room Access to the pool was great (right out a patio door), however, the rooms are very much in need of updating (dark, dingy, icky tile, etc. - also the room key doesn't work on the patio door so you have to go around to the front to get back in from the pool unless you leave it unlocked). The trip wasn't what I would call a disaster, however, if you are accustomed to the level of service at a Rtiz property, the El San Juan is not for you. We arrived at 2pm and were told our room may not be ready until 4 pm check -in but they would call us soon as it was ready. We rechecked at 3:45 and it still wasn't ready. By 5:00 we noticed others just walking in and receiving rooms right away and we still had not received a call. We again approached and only then were given a room right next to the elevator. It was only about 4 feet away from the elevator door that we passed it by. When we asked for another room they did not even try to hide their displeasure with our request. Throughout our stay we heard this same story over and over about the delays in checking in. We ended up on 4th floor 5 doors down from the elevator. Our beautiful view was the roof of the lobby with all its A/C equipment, etc. When I made reservations they said the only difference in the next room level up was that it was a higher floor. I just closed the drapes and never opened them again. The room itself was clean and an average size. It had been remodeled and had a tile floor which was much better to me than carpeting. However, the bathroom was very small, no tub, only a pedestal sink and a tiny shower that another reviewer aptly noted leaked all over the floor. There was no full length mirror in the room. Our package included 2 complimentary drinks and $25 casino credit. We did not receive the amenities at check-in, however, we requested it on our 2nd day and they complied. The first 2 nights we were awoken after the casino closed at 4 am by boisterous guests out in the hall. We complained via our cell phone because the room phone was dead (I had to unplug it to use the outlet for something else - because the room had no other outlets - and didn't plug it back in.) They would not listen to our concerns because we were not calling from a room. We heard doors slamming and people in the hall all through the 5 nights we were there - not peaceful at all. If you want a restful night you would have to bring earplugs with you. I will briefly list other cons. To get a lounge chair you had to get out there before 7 am. We learned that many come out early as 4 am to lay towels and claim chairs. Supposedly if a chair is unattended for 20 minutes the staff open it up, but we saw this happen only on our 4th day after many people complained. There was patio space for more chairs so I don't know why they had out such a limited number. Also, upon questioning staff we learned they had 4 chairs reserved for investors that were never occupied for 2 days. Bar service for both drinks and lunch was only for very patient guests. They were never busy, never in a hurry, totally apathetic to guest needs. The fitness center was average (thankfully, no extra charge for it). However, to get to it you had to sign in at the spa. One day the attendant did not even look up and greet us. Needless to say, there is no daily newspaper or turndown service, no robes, no slippers, no shower cap. They did have shampoo, conditioner, shower gel and lotion that smelled good. The onsite deli/pizzeria in the adjacent Galleria advertised to open at 11 am didn't open till 11:30 am. The food and service at the Palm Restaurant were superb. Our reservation had been lost and the manager treated us to dessert. The great table promised at the in-house Italian restaurant was actually right on top of a very noisy table and a family (the child behaved better than the adults on the other side). There was also a party of 12 in the room that was very, very loud. The food was excellent, the service below average and the ambiance poor. If you go there request a free standing table in the dining room with a window. The onsite Smoker's Suite supposed to open at 5 pm was still closed at 6 pm on Saturday night. Concierge said it was a concession and there was nothing they could do. Also, taxes and resort fees added almost $100 per day to the daily room rate. Pros - drink prices were very reasonable and very potent. The housekeeping staff did an excellent job. Management walking floor in hotel were friendly. In summary, if you love the way every staff person at the Ritz ends a sentence with my pleasure and you know they mean it - spend the extra and stay there. It is worth every dollar.

<Author>Cruzangirl
<Content>So So Stay at the El San juan My husband and I just returned yesterday from an anniversary weekend at the El San Juan. We have mixed feelings about our stay. So I will list the pros and then the cons. We think there are better choices, and although our stay was not awful, it wasn't great either.On past visits we have enjoyed the EL Convento (Boutique Hotel) and Marriott Condado much more than El San Juan.The pros:Our room was in the main building. It was spacious and decorated in an ultra modern decor. The room was clean. The bath products were nice. The linens and towels were above average quality. The room had a flat screen TV. The hotel pool area was very nice as was the adjacent beach.Dinner at the Japanese restaurant Yamato was excellent. The breakfast at the hotel's Las Terrazas restaurant was of good quality.Now the cons; the rooms are not sound proofed, so all night long we heard doors slamming, loud guests returning to their rooms and TV's from the adjacent rooms. We talked to some other guests who had experienced the same problem on another floor.In order to get a pool side lounge chair you must claim it by 7:30 am. There are not enough lounges for all of the guests. There was still plenty of empty space to place more chaise lounges, but instead people were hovering like vultures for lounge chairs to become available.Lastly the lunch at the grill took 2 hours from the time the order was taken until it arrived. Everyone was complaining. We ordered one salad and one burger. The waitress was apologetic and even brought us complimentary lemonade because it was getting to be a ridiculous wait. We are used to slow service in the Caribbean but this was beyond slow. Granted it was a holiday weekend, but that should have been taken into consideration when staffing the grill. We probably would not stay at the El San Juan again. There are better choices in San Juan.

<Author>LauraEL
<Content>Disappointing My husband and I (who travel extensively) were excited about visiting the El San Juan. Though our 7th trip to Puerto Rico, this was our first time in the Isla Verde area. The first 24 hours were pretty awful. The room (garden lanai -- and we paid mucho withtaxes and resort fees) was shabby with smudged walls and aging furniture. We found out later that these rooms had not yet been renovated. Our Hotel Directory binder was empty. When I enquired at the desk I was told that those rooms didn't get a directory. For $500+/night that seemed rather atrocious. There are signs everywhere that say the hotel is a non-smoking facility yet we had an ashtray and matches with the ESJ logo on our desk. The front desk seemed unconcerned. A private party the first night subjected us to loud rock music until late in the evening. The wireless internet was unbearable slow even when it worked, which wasn't often. The front desk staff were not particularly friendly. I was ready to go home after the first day.After that I warmed up a little to the place. It is true that there was little service there -- the room didn't get done until afternoon, there was no turndown service, no bathrobes -- the things you associate with luxury hotels. The bottle of water supplied would cost $10 if you used it. I did not have problems with bedbugs at all. The bed was comfortable and changed daily. The public areas are lovely, etc. Would I stay there again? Not sure. A different or more recently renovated room would be better, though the service seemed slow and sometimes non-existent.Breakfast was good and not too pricy, we only ate at the Agave Ranch which wasn't bad but (again) had an utter lack of any kind of service. I am NOT a whiner -- I have been all over everywhere and have many bases of comparison and the ESJ certainly came up short. Since many reviews are favorable, perhaps they need more consistency in how things are run.

<Author>junebugsrbig
<Content>No Problems for us...We liked this hotel My wife and I just returned from our Honeymoon. We went to St. Thomas and Purto Rico. We stayed at the El San Juan for 5 nights in late January/early February. We were very surprised to see the other reviews about poor service and bed bugs. We did not encounter any of this. We enjoyed our stay. I'm no travel expert, just an ordinary person who travels a couple times a year. Honestly, this hotel was very nice with above average service.There are 3 very nice looking bar areas when you walk in. A casino is immediately to the right. Everything was very well landscaped and kept up nicely. We stayed in the Garden Villas on the 100 level. NO PROBLEMS WITH BED BUGS!. Reports about thin walls are true. I have to admit that. However, it was not that bad for us. The pool area does get crowded and the hotel definitely picks up on the weekends. However, the pool area is not so crowded that its unbearable. There are 2 separate pool areas and 3 separate hot tub areas. The beach and Atlantic Ocean are only a few steps from the far pool area. We encountered no problems with getting 2 pool chairs and were alone in the hot tubs most of the time. The bartenders at the pool bar were very helpful and courtious. The pool is open 24 hours! You just have to bring your own towel after 5PM. The only thing they are strict on is attire in the lobby after 7PM. Slacks and shoes are required. No tanks, swimming trunks, shorts or flip flops after 7PM. I had to change into pants one night. There is even a little shopping galleria inside the hotel.Good luck getting a table at the Casino on Friday or Saturday night. Or getting into the night club Bravia. The lobby and casino are crowded on Friday  Saturday nights. Get to the craps table early! Performers come in and sing and play music and folks can dance and hang out at the bars after 7PM. Much different during weeknights. More low key atmosphere during the week nights.The service at this hotel was great! Our flight got us in at 1PM, and the concierge/reception was able to get us checked in early. Our returning flight did not leave until 7PM and they also let us check out late.(3PM) The bell man were very helpful and valet attendants were excellent. One did not speak english very well, but was able to run a co-worker down in a matter of seconds to help us out. The pool manager even got towels for us one day. We didn't have to leave our pool chairs. Be prepared to pay resort prices for the drinks though. We were new to the Island and everybody was very helpful with reccomendations for restaurants  sights to see! Old San Juan is a must!Overall, this was a very good hotel. Not 100% blown away by excellence, no. The room decor was not entirely modern. Couple of stains on the carpet and our safe did not work properly most nights. The TV's are not high tech modern flat screens, just your basic 19 inch Magnavox with basic cable and a VCR. No DVD. However, nothing is perfect. I'm not on vacation to watch TV or be blown away by fancy furniture/decor. No Bed Bugs in our room! Nobody slipped something into our drinks. We enjoyed our stay at this hotel. Very nice scenery. Great restaurants. Very helpful staff. We splurged one night and went to The Palm. Highly reccomended! Also, on the 10th floor is a neat cowboy/western theme type restaurant called Ranchers. Great food and atmosphere with a great view of the ocean. We would return to the El San Juan

<Author>d81976
<Content>Bustling Nightlife, Friendly Staff, Perfect for a wknd trip The El San Juan is a great hotel if you are looking for a quick, fun trip to PR. In particular, it is perfect for groups of friends looking to party. I actually went down with my wife, and we had a great time. I would not recommend the El San Juan if you are looking for a quiet stay. The club at the hotel is hopping, and it's not just tourists in there, a lot of locals partying as well. The lobby is bustling at night, and the casino has a lot of activity as well. If you are looking for a slower scene in PR, I would recommend either the Ritz (right down the road), or the El Conquistador. The hotel has just finished being refurbished. I had visited in June of this yr, and was very impressed with the improvement this time around. The La Vista class room basically looked exactly like it does on their website, and the bathroom was much nicer than than one that preceded the refurbishment. The only potential negatives I would point out are :1) The walls are kind of thin, so if you may get unlucky with a loud neighbor. We were thankful we had a neighbor that only made noise during the day.2) Although the El San Juan has the best party scene, the Ritz has better restaurants (including Il Mulino, which was very tasty btw) and a nicer casino.3) If you're looking to explore Old San Juan it is not walkable. You will need to take a cab r/t, which will run you about 20 each way. More important than the money is the time though, traffic can be an issue. I would not really recommend the hotel for more than a 3 day stay. All in all we were very happy with the El San Juan but would not recommend for all types of travellers.One other quick point on San Juan. Last time I was here I went to a restaurant called Marmelade, which was fantastic. This time we tried Parrot Club, and were unimpressed.

However, just sit at a table outside the inner circle and wear what you like. The locals, though, really dress up. There is dancing whenever and where ever the band plays! Fun atmosphere.Great lounge chairs and other seating by the pools (we loved these round beds shaped liked clamshells). And plenty to go around. Plenty of hammocks also. Chairs and umbrellas set up on beach at your request for no extra charge. Only a few vendors, not too disturbing. The only thing annoying was the LOUD house/club/lounge music with the most repetitive rhythm playing EVERYWHERE: the pool, the beach, the elevator, the hallways, the restaurants, the bathrooms. Because of the party atmosphere, it attracted many spring-breakers some of who, unfortunately, were in the rooms next to us. They were drunk and rowdy on Friday night. The hotel sent security up right away and they quieted down, but didn't prevent a repeat on Saturday night.
