<Author>cdt68
<Content>Fun, friendly, beautiful hotel We loved our stay at the El San Juan. We were looking for a place with a great pool, nice beach, and exciting night life. After doing research, we selected the El San Juan and were very happy with our choice. All staff were friendly and helpful, from the bellboys to the front desk to the pool waiters. The cleaning staff did a good job. Our room was always clean. Yes, the modern rooms are very different from the lobby, but everything worked fine and the beds are very comfortable with lots of pillows and nice linens. THe in room safe was nice. The pool areas are wonderful and the lounging beds are the best I've ever seen at any pool. The beach was very pretty and clean. The hotel offers a great variety of restaurants, though some are pricey. The Palm was wonderful, and we had very good sushi at Yamato twice. We didn't try the fancier Italian place, but the smaller Trattoria and Pizza place was good and not too expensive. We love the atmosphere in the lobby at night on the weekend. The salsa band was great and we had a wonderful time staying up dancing and visiting and watching the dancers. The lobby does have a dress code after 7:00 and rightfully so. It is a very elegant place. If, however, you are returning to the hotel from sightseeing or leaving for a more casual place that is no problem. There are several other entrances/ exits that are easily accesible and do not require you to walk through the lobby. I never saw anyone being hassled or made to feel uncomfortable. Drinks are very pricey all over the property. If you are looking to save some money, there are many options within just a few blocks of the hotel. We took a collapsible cooler and bought beer and drinks at the supermarket to take to the pool. No one at the hotel seemed to have a problem with that. We also saw others eating food from outside places at the pool and no one bothered them. Just outside the hotel entrance turn left and there is Lupi's Sports Grill. It is a great place to sit outside and watch the people walking on the sidewalk while enjoying reasonably priced food and drinks. Turn to the right and within the next several blocks you will find a supermarket and numerous fast food places (Subway, Wendy's, Burger King, Pizza Hut, Church's, etc.) as well as other restaurants. If you want to experience real Puerto Rican food, take a taxi to Casita Blanca. It is in the middle of a Puerto Rican neighborhood in an old refubished house. The food and atmosphere was great. Or head west from the hotel a few miles to Pinones. There are some beautiful beaches and little food stands with vendors selling what they call tacos, but are more like a fried meat pie filled with beef, chicken, crab, or shrimp. We visited fort El Moro which was fascinating and spent time walking around Old San Juan during the day and again at night (some very cool restaurants and night clubs there). There is a lot of talk about construction at the hotel and this is what we observed. The Veranda restaurant which is outside near the pool areas is being renovated. (The hotel informed us of this when we made our reservation.) They have put up decorated screens to block some of the view of the construction. It really wasn't a problem at the pool because it isn't right beside you and the noise was minimal. With the ocean breezes, fountains and waterfalls, and the pool music we were able to forget about the construction. The biggest disappointment is that the Oval Bar, the centerpiece of the lobby, is having some work done to it's counter tops and other upgrades. The hotel has actually walled it off while this is taking place. The walls have been painted and decorated, so there is no construction to see, but it hides the great chandelier and is strange having a temporary room in the middle of the grand lobby. Other than that, we just couldn't find much we didn't love about this place. This was our first trip to San Juan and the El San Juan Hotel and we can't wait to go back!

Up ahead there is a place where you can find a supermarket (can buy beer and snacks far less than the cost of the hotel), and ice cream shop, an excellent Spanish food restaurant (if you want to experience true Caribbean food, great prices too), a souvenir shop, and further ahead, before dominos. Is the breakfast and lunch restaurant. Really good food. My boyfriend and I had breakfast for a total of $16. Well, back to the hotel. The main pool was full of sand, as people don鈥檛 wash their feet before getting in. The second pool was relaxing and the cleanest. We had a great idea, to buy our own beer and snacks and keep them in the room. The hotel was charging $8 for a small can of Heineken. While a 6 pack of bottled ones, was $11. If you鈥檙e looking for a true Caribbean vacation, this is not the area or the hotel to stay. It is too Americanized. After I came back my co-worker (who is Puerto Rican) said next time head to Fajardo or the other side of the island, for true paradise.

Otherwise, the room was fine. We were also at the El San Juan when they had their Coors Light party that took up the area around the two main pools. The attendees at this party were generally not the paid guests of the hotel. I overheard a lot of people expressing their disappointment that the hotel was more interested in revenue from Coors Light instead of making sure that their guests were happy. The party went from noon until midnight and I can't imagine that anyone with rooms near the pools would be able to get any sleep until this ended (not a problem for most people, but a real problem for the families with children, I would imagine). Overall, I think that the hotel should decide if it wants to be a luxury hotel or if it is aiming at those in their 20's who are there to party. Everyone in Puerto Rico went out of their way to be nice to us. However, I wouldn't say that the service at the El San Juan was special in any way. Everyone was nice, but no one was exceptionally friendly or helpful.Overall, we enjoyed ourselves but I would not go back.

<Author>syceoner
<Content>The most honest review Ok, so I stayed in PR at the El San Juan from March 18th to the 25th in the upscale Garden rooms because my manipulative girlfriend was able to grab a free room upgrade with her expert travel skills. First the bad, when swimming at the beach the seaweed was overwhelming. It was probably the most seaweed I have ever encountered in my life. Although the water was nice and clear, it couldn't be fully enjoyed due to the seaweed invasion. Pricey, pricey, and pricey. Since my partner didnt take advantage of fully inclusive vacations (which is the only way to go) we needed to budget ourselves. This meant going to the supermercado to grab beers and food to control our bank accounts. On the resort you can count on $10 drinks, $50 breakfast bills, $140 dinner checks just to name a few. Your best bet is the go off resort to eat and drink becuase thats where you can find reasonable prices. The best part about the place was the pool area, simply sensational. By far it's a gem of the resort. This is the place to be during the day. Just thinking about it puts me in a state of tranquility. Another awe-inspiring element of the El San Juan is the lobby which includes numerous venues of entertainment, several bars and clubs along with a decent casino. If your a real gambler, dont count on this casino to satisfy your fix. It contains about four blackjack tables, four roulette tables, carribean stud table, craps table, and a bunch of slots. The worst part are the two miserable cocktail servers roaming around aimlessly who are terrible at their job. Overall I had a great time, but wouldn't consider going back. The best part about the whole trip was being with my ravishing girlfriend and time well spent with her. I love her.

<Content>Overpriced...Stay Somewhere Else This hotel has a beautiful lobby. It advertises that it is a 4 star property. It is priced four star but the service is a 1 star. What I disliked the most was the poor service. When I checked in the first night, I was placed in a small room with 2 queen beds and a view of the top of some part of the hotel. We were tired and went in for a shower the previous guest's hair was all over the bathroom floor. I called for housekeeping it took 4 more calls, a final call to the manager and 45 minutes to get a 300 dollar a night room cleaned. The next day I requested the king room and was moved in within 30 minutes. When I got in that room the air conditioner was broken and hair was on the sheets in the bed. I made another call concerning this and finally got the air fixed an hour later. Another day I needed an iron and ironing board it took 30 minutes to get it. The last day I called twice to get clean wash cloths by the time they came I had ran down the hall and grabbed some from a maid's cart and taken a 10 minute shower. This hotel is not big on service. They don't pride themselves in taking 4 star care of their customers. I will never come back again. Word to the Wise: stay somewhere reasonable and come enjoy the casino , the nice lobby and live entertainment. You will be glad you did.

If you want island fun and beautiful surroundings, do a lot of research before booking a hotel, especially one that costs what El San Juan does. <Author>bams4446
<Content>Needs a renovation of service We booked this vacation months ago, but found out the week before departing (from a disgruntled co-worker who had just returned) that the hotel was under major renovations -- with 2 of the 3 pools closed, and an abundance of noise. We contacted the hotel and asked for some form of reassurance/compensation and were told that we should have known about it and there was nothing to be done except cancel our trip and come back next year when the renovations are complete. Once we got our rooms, we were discouraged to find them dirty (hair that didn't belong to us, cigarettes on our porch), and not of a class you would expect to pay $300+ for. Additionally, the spa was closed. I rechecked their website and none of this is mentioned. The service issues were consistent, with waiters at the outside restaurant who couldn't remember orders, us returning to our room in the evenings to find that housekeeping had never come, a less than clean pool (the only one that was open) and a basically unaccommodating staff. The only bright spot were the bartenders, who were capable and nice -- perhaps because they realized that we had money to spend and would type well for deserving service. All in all, you can see that this place used to be nice, and the grounds are under major renovations so they should be nice again. However, if they can't manage basic service and cleanliness when they are less than half full they would need to renovate their entire staff to get back up to the class where they deserve the rates they seek. For similar rates, I would go to the Intercontinental next store that has a much better attitude, and you can still visit the ESJ at night. Or, splurge a bit more for the Ritz down the road which is in a different stratosphere of class and service.

Just further down the street is a Walgreens. This as again a very short walk from the hotel.I would stay here again.

Anyway, since we wanted to be relatively close to Old San Juan and the pier, we narrowed down our choices to the Marriott Sellaris, The Hilton Carribe and the Wyndham El San Juan and the Ritz-Carlton ALL of the on-line reviews were mixed for these four hotels and our travel agent said to go with the San Juan as she had stayed there before. (We were surprised about the mixed review of the Ritz-Carlton.) So, since we liked the idea that the El San Juan not only had a couple of pools, it also had one of the larger beaches plus the casino. For one night, we needed simply a standard room, non-smoking, two double beds ($425 a night) and the larger family confirmed TWO standard ADJOINING non-smoking rooms as they had a 16-, 8-, and 9-year old. Rosemarie, John and their 18-year old son arrived a day prior to us and had no difficulties. We arrived around 2 p.m., checked in, and left our bags in their storage area. The family of 5 had problems: There was only one room booked! They had their AmEx bill with them and showed the clerk that TWO rooms had been paid for. The hotel was very crowded, service was slow. It took about an hour to straighten out the mess, but they were still trying to find another room anywhere for our friends. Hungry and getting late, we decided to eat lunch overlooking the pool area. There were no other diners and we were seated immediately. Our drinks came quickly and we placed our orders (hamburgers, salads - the basics). It took close to 45 minutes to get lunch and it was somewhat expensive for what we ordered - 4 adults and 5 kids. Just a meal and a soda or water. No coffee, no desserts. Anyway, we got our bags and went to our room. It was warm, the A/C wasn't working and a ceiling tile was removed exposing wires. Just as we were about to call, two hotel personnel came in and called down to the desk to get our room changed. One informed us that she had previously alerted the desk staff that this room was under renovation and not to be used. My twins and I went to the pool and, an hour later!! my husband joined us as it took that long to find us a room. Our family of 5 friends FINALLY got two rooms but they were on two different floors! Being in the lobby, we could see many others who had arrived were having similar problems. The next morning, from 6:30 a.m. to 7:00 a.m., we were awakened by a loud, non-stop buzzing as if a construction crew had started working. It was Sunday and when I called the front desk to alert them, they said it wasn't construction and other guests had called and Security was handling it. The sound stopped shortly afterward, resumed briefly and finally stopped completely. Starting around that time we also heard planes taking off from the airport as the hotel is only about 5 or 10 minutes away and the flight pattern goes over the hotel. I had called the hotel directly when we booked and asked if there was any airplane noise and received a vague answer of not really. We really can't complain about airplane noise as we were fully aware of the hotel's location in relation to the airport and we decided to stay anyway. Be aware, this might really bother people staying here more than one night. Yes, the hotel, old but beautiful, under renovation according to staff, was charming and convenient. The pools and beach very nice. By the way, once the lobby cleared, I quietly asked the desk clerk if something could be done since we had been polite, quite and patient regarding our rooms. The manager sent us 2 free breakfast vouchers for the next day. NOTE: Breakfast buffet was $25 per person. Even with the 2 vouchers, we didn't feel like spending $50 for breakfast for the twins. We asked the Conceriege for a breakfast recommendation in Old San Juan that opened early. We and the family of 5, took a cab into Old San Juan; enjoyed a standard American type breakfast which amounted to about $25 for the 4 of us and about $30 for the other 5 . The restaurant was clean and service was quick. (At the hotel, they would have spent $125 for breakfast before tip.) We did some touring of Old San Juan and the Fort before heading back to the hotel to check out at noon and head for the pier. After vacation, Rosemarie checked her AmEx bill and found out the hotel had double billed them . . . We didn't hate the hotel/service, but we all agreed that if staying in San Juan again we would try another hotel next time.

<Author>Juliess31
<Content>So-so stay at the El San Juan We just spent our honeymoon at the El San Juan Hotel. We were there from June 1 until June 9, and have mixed reviews. I will start with the positives:1. The lobby is beautiful and a fun place to be if you are staying in the Isla Verde area. Wednesday through Sunday there is a band playing in the lobby and tons of vacationers and locals come to hang out and have fun. It is a great spot.2. Javier, the bartender at the lobby bar, is GREAT. He is attentive, makes good drinks, and is very friendly.3. We stayed in a Garden Lanai room, by the pool. The rooms are spacious and have nice, private balconies. I will discuss the negatives attached to the room below.4. We thought most of the staff was very nice (bartenders, pool staff, engineering staff, housekeeping, bellmen, valets, and many of the restaurants).5. There is a world class italian restaurant in the hotel that is worth every penny (can't remember the name, but its next to the Palm). 6. Because it was our honeymoon, the front desk attendant upgraded our room from what we had originally booked.7. It is very convenient that you can book tours directly in the lobby, and rent a car if you wish.8. My husband and I both had great spa massages. I had an 80 minute hot stone massage, which was unbelievable, and he had a 50 minute four hand massage (two therapists administer the massage at the same time - we like to call it a menagessage......)On to the negatives:1. Although they tell you check in is at 4:00, we were unable to check into our room the day we arrived until almost 5:00. This especially sucked, since we arrived at 11:00 in the morning. When we asked at the front desk if we could please have something different than the specific room pegged for us, we were told the hotel was sold out. We later found out the hotel was only at about 60% occupancy.2. The day after we arrived, the power went out (Friday) from about 5:45 pm until after 2:00 in the morning in the main building. Luckily for us, we were staying in the Garden Lanai building, and the electricity came on around 10:30 there. However, there were several problems associated with this. First, the backup generator, while powering the casino and ice machines (so people could continue to gamble and drink) didn't power the air conditioning (it was like 100 degrees). This is a bad choice of what to provide power to in an emergency. Also, in the garden lanai building, NONE of the emergency hallway lights worked. It was pitch black and seemingly dangerous. We found an elderly woman kind of stuck in the stairwell not knowing what to do - luckily she was staying next door to us so we all walked to our room together. Also, there were teenagers running up and down the dark hallways, and security was nowhere to be seen. We actually went to the pharmacy and bought our own flashlights, feeling quite unsafe.3. There are proms at the hotel EVERY night! It appears the kids are allowed to rent rooms as well, so there are teenagers all over the place, using all the hottubs, being drunk, and generally making the resort less relaxing than it should be.4. Our shower didn't work correctly (there was a bunch of water trapped between the tub liner and the tub). It would leak out with a foul odor, and it took us three front desk calls to get engineering to come to the room. The engineer who did come to the room, Roberto, was great, and basically offered to come to our room every time it leaked and clean it up. Other than that, we were not given a new room or anything.5. The rooms need some sprucing up - definitely some wear and tear due to age. I hear a renovation is going to begin in six months.6. The restaurant The Ranch has a horrible manager. We were there at 5:20, told they opened at 5:30, and to wait ten minutes while they had their staff meeting. At 5:50, we decided to just leave - the manager can't seem to get her restaurant open on time, and didn't understand that she should try to prevent us from leaving and apologize. Overall, we would be unlikely to stay at this hotel agian, although we didn't think it was as awful as the other reviews indicated.On to the negatives:

The staff was so nice , they went out of their way to make you happy, the guest rooms were immaculate the lobby bathrooms, you could eat off the floor. <Author>kdmc
<Content>Thumbs up A 3-night getaway at the El San Juan in late January ... it was idyllic. We sent an email ahead of time requesting an early check-in. They wouldn't promise but said they'd try. Sure enough, a room was ready, and it was lovely. A garden room with a private patio and hot tub (somewhat worn but it worked). The room itself was spotless, charming and spacious. We had a sitting area, a huge walk-in closet, comfortable bed, more bureau space than we could use. We had no complaints. The folks at the front desk were helpful and polite. The lobby is drop-dead gorgeous. We spent an hour one evening there just watching the people go by. We only tried one of the restaurants -- for lunch, delicious but expensive, though really what we'd expect to pay at a similar restaurant in Washington (ditto for the drinks at the bars). The pool area is expansive and well-designed, never felt crowded despite the high season. Same for the beach. I'd read the many reviews of the El San Juan ahead of time and seriously considered changing hotels. I'm so glad we didn't. The El San Juan is beautiful, historic and well worth the tariff.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Vacation My boyfriend and I stayed at the El San Juan for a long weekend in February. We booked 2 weeks before we left. The prices were high but Puerto Rico seemed a good choice for a long weekend. After booking I read some of the reviews on this site and to say the least I was nervous. However, we did not cancel as friends and family had been to the El San Juan in the past and loved it. I must say that I worried over nothing. Those who read this should know that my boyfriend and I are in our mid 30's, from NY and both have high paying jobs. We travel at least 3 times a year and stay at 4 and 5 star hotels.There are a lot of complaints about the rooms on this site. Ours was fine. Afterall, how much time do you spend in the room? I would not say that the room was a $455/night room however it was more than adequate and extremely comfortable and clean. For those who complain about the noise of the planes, I suggest that you do not stay in Isla Verde as the airport is literally 5 minutes away. We had a very nice view from our room, the ocean to the left and the mountains to the right. Our patio was very nice and we often sat there when we were getting ready and had a cocktail. I agree that the room is not a 5 star room but you are not paying for the room, you are paying for the hotel. The rooms do need an updating but it is still nice and I would definitely stay here again. On this site I've read complaints about the grounds. THe grounds are gorgeous. Yes, once in awhile you see some leaves floating in the pool but what do you expect when there are so many trees? Come on people this is a beach resort. There is going to be sand and leaves in the pool once in awhile.The hotel was beautiful. It is the hub of social life in San Juan. The club was alike many other clubs except that there are 2 floors with different music playing on each floor. The drinks are small at the club and cost approx $7.50. The hotel bars are beautiful. I drink Grey Goose and it costs $10 a drink. If you are from NY this is reasonable and it also is a decent sized drink. For those of you who are used to buy backs at bars, don't expect any. My boyfriend is a huge tipper (not a 20% tipper, closer to 30-40%)and we did not get one free drink.The Salsa dancing and music every night is great. It really makes you feel like you are on vacation and makes you want to learn how to do it. I loved sitting at the bar after dinner, having a drink and watching people dance.Every dinner that we had was terrific. The Palm, the Italian restaurant and the Mexican restaurant were all very good. Yes, the Palm and the Italian restaurant are not cheap but they are not any more expensive than the places we go to in NY for a nice dinner. It is not going to be cheap if you are eating lobster and steak for dinner. The Mexican Restaurant was reasonable. We had the breakfast buffet once. Yes it was expensive, $60 with tip. However, it is no different than any other Resort buffet breakfast I've been to. We are not big breakfast people but if you are, it was good. The food that you order at the pool was horrendous. For lunch one day I ordered a $16 turkey sandwich and it was gross. It seemed as though it was Oscar Meyer turkey. Yuck. My boyfriend had a hamburger which was okay but not for $18. We had burgers at the pizza place one day and they were huge and good.It was appx $10 a burger. The pizza was okay. For those of you who feel like walking, Lupi's is good for lunch. It is next door to the left of the hotel. Also if you make a right outside the hotel there is every fast food restaurant you can think of.I enjoyed the Casino. I think that it is great that they have $5 and $10 tables. That does not happen in Atlantic City. My biggest complaint about the trip were the dealers. Many were down right rude. Also if you play blackjack make sure you count your cards because on 2 occasions the dealer went to take my money when I had won the hand. However, if you sit at a table with a good crowd the dealers should not bother you. And don't forget... you are on vacation, relax.Overall, I found the service great, the restaurants great, the room sufficient and the hotel beautiful. I think that anyone can find something to complain about anywhere if they look for it. I can't wait to go back.

<Content>Mixed review of the Wyndham ESJ My wife and I just returned from a week at the Wyndham ESJ and had a mixed experience. I called back and asked to speak with the front desk manager, and presto, the clerk picked up the phone and told me that our room was ready and a key was promptly produced.Room: Below averageI concur with the other posters who said that the rooms were shabby. Our room (818), while clean, had a moldy smell and the carpet was worn in several places. The rooms could really use an upgrade. People considering this hotel should also note that a busy airport runway is located only a few hundred yards away from the hotel and during peak air traffic hours, the noise can be deafening. Maid service was prompt and reliable. The room was always cleaned by mid-afternoon. In summary, I expect a much nicer room for $275/night (all-in). Pool: ExcellentThe pool area is fantastic. The grounds are clean and well-maintained. The pool waitstaff is friendly and attentive, but never pushy. I often brought my own beer to the pool and was never hassled. My only complaint about the pool is that bad music was constantly being played at a high volume - it sounded like soft porn music. We asked the staff to turn it down a couple of times and they complied. The ocean beach is also nice and located just outside the pool area.Casino and Bar: ExcellentThis is what makes the Wyndham ESJ worth the money. On Thursday-Saturday, the stunning lobby, bars and casino explode with music, dancing and action. I really can't describe it - you need to see it to believe it. We were playing Blackjack next to Derek Jeter one night. We also bumped into Governor Pataki (NY) in the lobby.Restaurants: GoodThe Japanese place (Yamato) is very good and the teppanyaki chefs are entertaining. The food is decent at the poolside cafe and Palm is a solid steakhouse. These places are all very pricey - nine bucks for a rum punch! Go across the street and try Mi Casita and Metropole for reasonable, authentic Puerto Rican and Cuban fare, respectively.Gym: ExcellentPlently of treadmills and a nice assortment of machines and free weights. We had a really good vacation, but the next time, I will probably stay at the Intercontinental (for a nicer, less expensive room) and party at the Wyndhan ESJ.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Do yourself a favor, don't stay here. The hotel is not terrible, but this is only because the pool and beach are very nice (although the cushions on the lounge chairs need replacing), the lobby is stunning and the casino retains a sense of mid century elegance that is not found everywhere. You can enjoy those things, however, without staying here and save yourself a lot of aggravation. The hotel is not inexpensive; in high season rooms are $350/night. This was my second stay here, and it was complimentary due to complaints about problems the first time around.The main problems are the grudging service from front desk staff, which apparently stems from hotel policy, and the shabbiness of the rooms. The first time we stayed (March 2005), we had paid $350 for the first night in advance and arrived around 8pm. We were told there was no room for us, and given a room that was the livingroom of a suite, and had no bed. It had a small murphy bed on the floor, and we slept there. When I raised the issue of being charged $350 to sleep in a room with no bed with management the next day, I was told that the hotel does not accommodate the guests and that by virtue of signing the registration card I had agreed to pay $350 for whatever sleeping arrangement they gave me. I contested the charge, raised the issue with Wyndham International management, and received a certificate for two free nights. This time around we arrived early, at about noon, and were told that the hotel was overbooked and that we could check in starting at four. I gave them my certificate for a free stay and a letter from management that said that we were entitled to a room upgrade. The first time I was here was during the high season, but this is off-season and it was apparent from the pool area that the hotel was not full. But fine, we went to the pool to await check in. When I returned to the desk at four, I was told that the room still was not ready, and I asked about the upgrade. I was told that the room was a high floor room, and to come back between four and five. I returned at five, still no room. I returned at five-thirty, and finally was checked in to a room on the fourth floor directly over the roof and the air conditioning unit. I would not have thought it was an upgrade, and it was not a high floor. The room itself was spacious, but had the same issues that our room had the last time around: musty smelling rattan dresser (that you really can't put clothing in), outside furniture that is visibly very dirty, stains on carpet and curtains, musty smelling bathroom. One bedside lamp did not work properly.Poolside service was entirely absent; in two days sitting by the pool we were not approached by a waiter once. Not one time. In addition, our minibar was never refilled. It appears that the management is simply unaware that it is in a service industry, and that this is a for-profit business.This all may seem picky, but remember it is not an economy hotel, and bills itself as a luxury resort. I recommend that you stay elsewhere (the nearby Ritz-Carlton, for instance), and visit the lobby and casino in the evening.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great stay I just returned today and thought it be best to share my thoughts while it's fresh in my head. Ok, here is the scoop on the El San Juan. It's in Isla Verde, which is a beach community in San Juan. Apparently a wealthier area of Puerto Ruco. Lots of hotels and high rise apartment buildings. Althought lacking the charm of Old San Juan, the area has plenty of dinning options and amentities not too mention it's five mintues from the airport. Old San Juan is only a 15 minute cab ride away so it's very convenient. The resort is located on a the beach in Isla Verde. The water is nice, but not the crystal clear caribbean water you may find in other areas of the island. Don't get me worng the water is still very nice and it seems to get a pretty good surf. The beach was very nice with white sand.The resort itself is gorgeous. The grounds and and lobby are top notch. The lobby is simply one of the nicest hotel lobbies I have ever been in. It has elegance and a rich latin quality about it. Looks like it belongs in a movie. It is the place to be Thursday through Sarurday. The lobby is electric with classy locals and tourists alike. The casino was very nice and the dealers looked and acted very professional. The best live latin music and the hottest nightclub in all of puerto Rico are right there. People are dressed to impress and the atmosphere is perfect, very rich and very old world. There is something for everybody right there. There are several fine dinning options at the hotel as well, but the prices are through the roof. Nice places, but not worth spending that kind of money when Puerto Rico is filled with great restaruants all over particularly in Old San Juan.The pool and facilaties are beautiful. Swim up bar, plenty of lounge chairs and several hot-tubs. Prices for drinks and food are high and really not worth it. $22 for two avaerage pina colatas in small plastic cups. Service overall around the resort was very pleseant.We ran into a few problems with the front desk. They messed up on our billing and provided us incorrect and inconsistent information. We were not pleased, but we got the situation corrected. I think they need to get a refresher course in customer service. This is not the days inn hotel at some airpot. This is a resort where people are spending a lot of money and want good quality service. The rooms - bottom line, are Ok. They certainly do not match the ambience and cleanliess of the lobby. The rooms are spacious, but they are in desperate need of a face lift. This place is old and it's starting to show. Apparently Wyndham just sold it to Blackstone and they intend to put $140 million into renovating all the rooms. We'll see? Don't get me wrong, the rooms are not intolerable, they're just not worth the money. People love the El San Juan becasue of the grounds, ambience, nightlife and amenities. That's why we stayed there and it was a good choice. We loved it and I would return just for that.

<Author>aknannie
<Content>Trade-off The El San Juan is a treasure, but a mixed bag, to say the least. First of all, there is nothing like it, anywhere. The main bar is the extravagance you see as you enter this grand hotel. The casino is nearby on the first floor, as well as the music, tables and several of the restaurants (tucked away discretely). It is a scene! Stay here if you want a taste of the real culture of PR, and enjoy a good time! The local people come here to dress up and party...as do the guests (from other hotels, too). We were there with another couple, all in our 50's...every age from 20's up come to dance, party and gamble. We had dinner at The Palm...wonderful. The menu looks expensive, but isn't when you share...if you're familiar with this restaurant in other locations, lots of people do share the sides, too...who wants to have a 24 Oz. steak? The Italian restaurant is very good, too. Now, the down side. The rooms are in varying states of refurbishment, I guess. Where the rooms pictured on the website are, I have no idea. Our room was a disgrace for a high end chain like Wyndham. Dreary,with draperies from the 70's shredded on the inside. Old bed and carpet. But it was clean. Other people we met (and the couple we went with) all changed rooms 2 or 3 times. What to do? When we left, they had just started painting and redoing some rooms on our floor. I asked at checkout, why the rooms were so awful. Receptionist said that they redid rooms as Wyndham sent money for refurbishment. That was in Jan.2005. From the sound of other comments made last month, they haven't finished. The Ritz Carlton, a few doors down is, lovely. We stayed there one night in a standard room (cancelled flight)..fabulous bed and linens and all you'd expect from a Ritz. But a little corporate and quiet...you could be anywhere. We're going back this Jan., but can't decide..what to do? Maybe this review will help you decide where you'd rather stay.Travel PS- Dining in San Juan is excellent...explore. Also, You can walk from the El San Juan to The Ritz...But NOT on the beach at night. You're in a city, even if you don't feel that you are. Be safe, and enjoy.

Yes, there is a dress code for the lobby after a certain time, but we didn't find it to be a problem. We both wore jeans one night and no one said a word to us. A lot of people come to that hotel in the evening to go the club, casino or to hear the live band play in the bar area. It was really a good time.We went to Old San Juan and had a good time. Everyone was friendly, and you do not need to speak Spanish there. I did not meet 1 person who did not speak English. Some of the reviews mentioned that the town is kind of dirty. That is true, but I think if you can over look that you will be fine. Have you ever been to the streets of Newark? I think they are a lot dirtier.I wish we had more time there because there was so much more we wanted to see. We will definitely go back and I would recommend both the hotel and San Juan. I would prefer Aruba to Puerto Rico as a carribean island. We spent 8 days throughout the various areas of PR and dollar for dollar, I spent more money there than I ever spend in Aruba. But the cultural experience I walked away was a good one because as a healthcare worker, I can now understand the relationships, living conditions, emotions, and why we see the behaviors we see. Put it on your list of carribean islands to see but don't make it for any longer than 3-4 days---that will give you enough of a taste of the island.

<Rating>3	4	4	-1	4	-1	2	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great R My wife and I recently spent our fourth wedding anniversary in Puerto Rico from August 2nd to August 5th. We were both looking for a quick getaway to spend some time on the beach, relax and to get away from our children. Initially, we were booked to stay at the Wyndham El Conquistador. I am sure it is a very nice resort but when we learned that it would take us 15 minutes to get to the beach and possibly over an hour to get there from the airport we decided to switch. We decided to move our reservation to the El San Juan in the Isla Verde section of PR. It was right on the beach and it was recommended to us by family. Let me start by saying that was a great move. We landed at 11:05 and we were on the beach by 12:15. Our room was not ready until 1:30, two and a half hours earlier than check-in, so our bags were checked and brought to us later while we relaxed. The hotel is very close to the airport so after 10 minutes and a $9 fare we were where we wanted to be. The hotel itself is an older hot spot of SJ life. The lobby was gorgeous and a fun place to be at night. Guests of many other hotels in the area and locals come for drinks here at night, Thursday night being the biggest evening by far. Food and Drink- The restaurants are top notch. We ate dinner at the Italian restaurant, the Palm steakhouse and the Asian restaurant. All the reviews I read complained about the prices and while they were high, they were not highway robbery. You paid for top quality food and service. It was expensive, NYC prices, but the food was excellent and worth every penny. Service was equally as good. We also ate at the pizza place and had a very nice lunch that was reasonably priced. As one might expect, drinks were pricey but I think when you are traveling to a resort you need to set your expectations properly. If you think you are going to get off cheap you're better off staying at a Holiday Inn. Beers were $6 and mixed drinks closer to $7-8 but that is what you would pay at most restaurants or bars so I don't see a need to get bent out of shape about it. If it that much of a problem, go buy a 12 pack and a bottle of rum from the grocery store down the street. It costs $25! Local restaurants, Metropol in particular, were good places for good regional food and a break from resort prices. Accommodations- They were nice, not spectacular. I suppose if it rained the whole time I was there and I was forced to be confined in my room I would have more bad things to say about them as cabin fever set in and the booze ran out but we had beautiful weather (more on this later) so it was not a problem. Furthermore, I did not go to PR to sit in my room all day nor should anyone else. We had a standard room with a king bed. The rooms, quite simply put, were clean, neat and functional but need updating. The bathrooms must have been redone recently as they were nicely appointed and nicely decorated. The room could have used a coat of paint, new carpet and a new bedspread but there was truly nothing wrong with it. Perhaps I could have requested a nicer room if I cared to complain but I had the vacation mindset and I did not want to complain like a typical NYer. They were clean and functional. The balcony was a little beat up. One last note on the rooms: remember, you are close to the airport. While it is not busy all night, flights leave early in the AM and you can hear them in the room. Light sleepers might want some earplugs.Service- I read a lot of reviews complaining about the attitudes of the staff. I found them to be completely and totally unfounded. The staff and people were all wonderfully polite and helpful. I also think if you are polite and respectful, you should get the same in return. This was true in PR and at the Wyndham. Weather- Every place looks better when it is sunny and PR is no exception. Despite numerous forecasts for rain every day for a month, the only adverse weather we had was a minute of rain when we landed and a cloudy day. Otherwise it was beautiful. That certainly has a lot to do with my positive review! I am sure if it rained for four days I would be complaining a lot more! Hotel grounds- The beach is right there and it is white sand with warm, calm water. No hawkers peddling there wares walking up and down the beach. The pools were very nice, with swim up bars and great chaise lounges. I hope this review helps someone out there. I thoroughly enjoyed my trip. While the trip was nice and perfect in many ways, I am not sure I would go back to Puerto Rico. It is a fairly developed country and it loses some of that island charm that is more abundant in the smaller Caribbean islands. But if you are looking for some rest and relaxation, this trip was great. As an aside, I usually don't like to write these types reviews as I find they are inherently biased. People who have horrible experiences are more likely to go on a discussion board and bash the hell out of a place or a hotel if they had a bad experience. So for every five bad reviews, you might get one good one. It doesn't paint a fair picture. Those people are more than entitled to express their opinion but I think someone who has an average or above average trip should be as quick to review a trip as well as someone who did not. Thanks.

<Content>Mixed Review We just returned from our vacation in Puerto Rico. The last 3 days we spent at the Wyndham El San Juan Hotel and Casino. We were all in comfortable clothing (shorts, sandals, etc.). Boy did we feel underdressed when we walked into the lobby of this hotel. Maybe it was because of this that we were checked in VERY quickly! Our friend was parking the car, so 2 of the kids (16 and 14) sat in the lobby right by the Front Desk to wait on him so they could show him to the room. While they were waiting, a Security Guard came up and told them they had to leave because of their attire - their is a strict dress code after 7 PM in the lobby. They explained that they were waiting for their dad. The Security Guard said they had 5 minutes and then they had to leave. Thank goodness their dad walked up just after the Security Guard. The rooms are definitely not up to the Wyndham standards that I am used to. We had a great view of the pool and the ocean. One great safety concern that I had was the fact the the sliding glass door opened VERY EASILY and although there was a concrete railing on the other side of the door, it would not take anything for a child to open the door. The bathrooms were VERY small (just big enough for 1 person) and definitely showed signs of age!!!!! Our bathroom had plaster falling off the ceiling, and the bathtub / shower enclosure was so narrw that if you had a weight problem you might not have been able to use it. The bathtub had been recovered and their was water trapped underneath it. When you stepped in you felt as if you were on a waterbed. We called Engineering, who came up quickly, slit the plastic cover to release the water and glued it up. However, the next morning it was back to the way it was before. Due to the fact that the door to the bathroom had slats in it - there was NO PRIVACY whatsoever. As for sound proofing in the rooms - there was none. You could clearly hear EVERYTHING that was going on in the rooms around you. My daughter and 2 other teenage girls we were traveling with all had to share a room since they only allowed 4 people in a room and they have no roll-away beds available. They were on the same floor as us, but a few rooms down. When I asked why they were so tired the second day, they said that they were up all night because the people next door were having sex all night long. They got to listen to moaning, groaning, and the bed banging on the wall! Then the room on the other side of them had a little baby who cried all night long! This is not exactly something the front desk could do anything about! The lobby was gorgeous - with wood and chandeliers everywhere! And it came alive at night! There was live bands, Salsa dancing, a man rolling hand made cigars, and of course - the casino! The food was mixed. We ate at the Italian Restaurant on night and had a fabulous dinner! The service was great and the food was wonderful. We ordered dessert from Room Service one night and were terribly disappointed and it was very expensive - $25 for 3 pieces. The Carrot Cake was dry, as was the triple layer cake and the Flan was rubbery. The Deli in the Galleria was very expensive - $14.95 for a cheeseburger and $12.95 for a Tuna Sandwich. The pool and the beach are fabulous! Overall, the lobby is beautiful, the casino is fun, the entertainment is great, but the rooms (which is what you are paying $225 per night and up for) were a total disappointment.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place to visit, but.... Just got back from 5 nights celebrating a friends birthday. The good: Hotel lobby is beautiful (old world opulence and charm). The two rooms I saw had large wet spots (2' diameter) on the rug from air conditioner condensation which gave them a musty/moldy smell (we were told there was nothing they could do to fix the problem). Bedspreads had miscellaneous stains on them (I don't want to know). Poor soundproofing- you can hear conversations in the neighboring rooms, phones ringing, room service and maid carts moving down the halls, vacuuming (at 7am) and of course the airplanes. My room actually vibrated from pipes whenever the room above used their shower or opened their closet slider! We were all supposed to get upgraded and were told they were unavailable because the hotel was sold out (I called a reservation line and found this to be a lie). My friends used the spa- massage  manicure and were overcharged even though they presented a buy one service get one at half price coupon all guests were given at the pool.  Unable to get into my room until 4:30pm (suprising because check-out is at noon and it is almost impossible to get a late check-out).Lastly, when I checked out, the woman at the front desk never even asked how was your stay, etc. - a basic customer service question.In summary: With some renovations and more attention to customer service, this hotel can be restored to its former grandeur. If you can get by the above issues, enjoy. If not, stay somewhere else and visit on a Friday or Saturday night for great people-watching.

<Author>superyooch
<Content>Some flaws but not as bad as every one says!!! I just got back from my trip to PR on Wednesday. I have to say I had THE MOST WONDERFUL TIME! I will try to write a detailed review because I know how much reviews help a traveller out. I stayed at the Wyndham El San Juan for 3 nights. Check in time for the hotel is 4:00 pm so please be prepared to wait if you get there any earlier especially if you have preferences (king size bed/ non-smoking...etc). I arrived at the hotel around noon and was told that there were no rooms available because housekeeping did not get a chance to clean them yet (check out time is noon). I left them my cell number and the bell boy took our luggage and locked it in a room where it was filled with other people's luggage. Apparently, this was a common occurrence. I wasn't to annoyed because there were a lot of things to do around the hotel. We walked around the pool grounds, the beach and explored the different shops and restaurants. We had a snack and played in the casino to kill some time. I got the call around 2:20 and was told that my room was ready. The hotel-The hotel is about a 7-10 minute cab ride from the San Juan airport. The cab costed us 9 bucks (.50 for each piece of luggage). I loved that the cab ride was short. When you first see the hotel, the exterior is nothing special. It's actually very plain and you begin to question whether or not you made the right choice. However, once you enter the hotel lobby, you're immediately awestrucken by the lobby. The lobby is furnished with dark wooden furniture with a bar and a huge chandalier as it's center piece. There are a numberous amount of chairs and tables around the lobby for people to lounge and people watch. There is a dress code if you plan on lounging in the lobby or casino, and if you're eating at the restaurants in the lobby. If you're just passing through, they didn't say anything. We didn't have a problem being scolded.The rooms-We were told that the last time the rooms were renovated was in 1988. That's about 20 years ago so there is bound to be some wear and tear. The carpet in the hallway are a bit dirty but I didn't care because I wasn't sleeping on them or walking on them barefoot. The room I stayed in had a balcony with 2 chairs (dirty) but we never used it. We were hardly in the room. There was a ceiling fan which was nice. However the rooms can get quite cold. Housekeeping always sets the thermostat to 70 degrees with the ceiling fan on high. We tried to set it lower because it does get quite cold, but the room just got humid. I'm guessing 70 degrees is the happy medium. The room really is no fuss. It had the regulars: bed, armoire with tv, nightstand, etc. My boyfriend and I are not picky people so long the bed/bathroom were clean and they were. The bathroom was also no fuss. Toilet seat, sink and a bath tub with shower head. The carpet in the room were stained so we opted not to walk around barefoot. I have definitely stayed at better places but at the same time I could see how the hotel is a 5 star hotel back in the early 90s. If you're used to present time 5 star hotels, I would have to say you would be disappointed unless you were staying at a suite. The restaurants at the hotel-We ate at the Veranda restaurant near the pool. DO NOT eat outdoors. We ate inside and watched the people outside get bombarded with pigeons and baby crows. It was pretty unappetizing. We ate there during lunch time and I guess they were short staffed so it took a while for the busboys to clear the table which meant feast time for those birds. The food was mediocre and overpriced like any restaurant in a hotel. I had the cobb salad and my bf had the calamari. My advice is to stick with the no nonsense, can't mess up type of food. The calamari was horrible. We never went back there again. We also ate at the Bistro. It's the only hotel that is opened passed midnight. The food is pretty good but again expensive. The prices increase when they start using a late night menu. We also ate at the Palm Steakhouse which was delicious. It was a bit pricey but we were on vacation and wanted to splurge a little. The service was excellent and we left stuffed and satisfied.The restaurants around the hotel-We ate at Edith's Cafe. Excellent authentic Puerto Rican food. Really cheap too. Another restaurant we tried was breakfast at Piu Bella's. The food was mediocre but decently priced. I wasn't particularly impressed with the restaurant but it was a lot cheaper than the restaurants in the hotel. Pools/Beach-We didn't hang around the pool during our stay but it looked very nice. There were 2 pools and 1 hot tub. It never looked crowded, I'm guessing because the beach is a few feet away. The beach is very nice and clean. The water is always warm! There's chaise lounges you can lay on and the cabana boy will bring it to whatever spot you want to sunbathe at. A beach in the hotel's backyard is definitely a big plus for me.Excursions-I booked 2 tours from GSI tours who had a booth in the Wyndham (near the entrance to the pool). The lady that was there was very helpful and explained everything to us. I did the Biobay kayaking tour in Fajardo for $88.00/person. THIS IS A MUST. The $88.00 will buy you round trip transportation to Fajardo (about 1.5 hours from Isla Verde), the biobay tour and some snacks after the trip. The tour guides are excellent on this trip. They were funny and informative. I do have to warn you that this is a kayaking tour. You will be kayaking for a good amount of time in the dark until you reach the biobay. The reason for this is because power boats harm the biobay so this tour company does not offer that service. I also booked the Old San Juan/Bacardi Distillery/El Morro Fort for $40.00/person. I loved this tour because you learn alot about the culture and history about PR. I absolutely loved Old San Juan. It was such a cute city! There are tons of shops and restaurants and you can easily kill a whole day there. We decided not to leave with the tour when we got dropped off at Old San Juan (it was the last stop of the tour) because they only give you an hour to walk/shop/eat. I didn't think that was enough time. We took a cab ride back to our hotel from Old San Juan and it was a flat rate of $16.00, which isn't too bad if you just wanted to go to Old San Juan on your own. I'm sure I could've gotten better deals on the tour but we wanted to have a sense of security that we would be going with an organized group. Other hotels-We went to the Intercontinental and Ritz Carlton just to compare the hotels. They were both very nice and newer than the Wyndham. However, I did notice that the lobby at both hotels were dead. At Wyndham El San Juan, the lobby was always busy with people having drinks and lounging. A dealer at the casino told me that this was where the local rich people dress up and hang out at. All in all, I loved PR and I felt that staying at the Wnydham was an integral part of that. The location was nice and the service was excellent. However, when I do visit PR again, I will be staying in the Condado area. We passed by on our way to Old San Juan and it looked more tourist oriented and had more shops/restaurants whereas in Isla Verde, it's more relaxed.

<Author>malaplan
<Content>Not particularly family friendly I stayed with my family (wife, 1 toddler son) at the Wyndham in May 2005. It was part of a business trip and we stayed the better part of a week.The location, 5 minutes from the airport, was both good and bad. It was right on the beach in Isla Verde and a short drives (about $15-16 taxi fare to Old San Juan and the Plaza Las Americas) from major sites. Because of its proximity to the airport, there was frequent noise from planes landing and taking off.The facilities, overall, were fantastic - with a casino just off the lobby, good sized rooms, beautiful pools, and multiple (expensive) restaurants on-site. There are several hotels/restaurants within walking distance and a strip mall with very reasonably priced restaurants and a grocery store a 5 minute walk away. Some areas of the resort were very shabby, with a clearly visible office/now storage room in disrepair, not far from the pool area. Their business center was well-equipped.Apparently Puerto Rico allows smoking in public areas, and the first thing noticed is the smell of smoke. The hotel is a busy one, with our one week there showing a graduation, a prom dance, TV cameras and a local celebrity, and a live band which played (very loudly) into the night.Service is spotty, from downright poor (front desk, who basically do not do as promised - we waited 4 hours for a room and 1 hour for our luggage and they never notified us about the room although they requested a cell phone number for that purpose) to passable (maid service - our room was not the cleanest we've been in) to excellent (room service and concierge). They did not seem to be interested in feedback as customer satisfaction questionnaires did not seem readily available.Also, I would caution you about the tipping service - often tips are included in the restaurant bill and room service, but this feature is spotty with some restaurants having it and some not. If you are impressed by the service and want to tip above the included gratuity, by all means do, but check your bill carefully to see if it is or not.All told, a great place for a short stay (it's very expensive) and you're not going with a family (it's exciting and a place to party). But if you're going with a family, it might not be a ideal place.

<Author>milhouse
<Content>Hip Lobby -- Disgusting Rooms Stayed at the WESJ after a 7 day cruise and have to say that most reviews of this hotel hit the nail right on the head. The a/c unit dripped water constantly right into the middle of the room leaving a big puddle (I kid you not). The soundproofing for these rooms is simply ridiculous -- even had all the other problems not occurred, it would have been impossible to get a night's sleep at this hotel. We heard everything happening on our floor (the 8th) the entire night. When we complained to hotel management of these problems and notified them that we wanted to leave early they charged us $75 for early departure. While I realize that we had booked via the internet and chosen the non-refundable rate, I had no idea what kind of hellish room we would be getting. I chose the non-refundable rate with the understanding that the room we would be getting would be of a certain resort standard. The room we received barely met cheap motel standards and the $75 charged to be allowed to leave this dump-with-a-beautiful-lobby is asinine. Do yourself a favor and check yourself in at the Ritz -- it's where we moved to and we were quite happy with our accomodations. If we ever visit PR again (doubtful) I would only consider the Ritz or the El Convento Hotel in Old San Juan (we stayed there 1 night before our 7 day cruise).

The comments about service are probably accurate. It鈥檚 ok if you are fine w/self service, which for the most part we are, but if you really want a 4 or 5 star service experience you won鈥檛 find it here. The pool area is nice and spacious and you can be at the pool w/a view of the ocean. The pool/beach area is important criteria for me and I was happy here and the outside bar service was good. We spent only a little time on the beach after jet skiing. We took over some lounges and an umbrella and I was annoyed when I watched an employee talk to my husband and take the umbrella that other guests had left for us away. Once I got out of the water I found out that it鈥檚 $10 to have an umbrella on the beach, which I think is ridiculous given that I鈥檓 already a guest at the hotel but since we weren鈥檛 staying at the beach long I didn鈥檛 make it an issue. There is security around the pool and I did not find this to be an issue. I like that only guests are allowed in the pool area. I found outside pool area to be better and more spacious than that of the Ritz and could see people staying at other hotels looking to spend time at this pool instead. The lobby was nice but after reading about how great it was I didn鈥檛 find it that grand. We only spent a little time in the casino and it was also fine. We didn鈥檛 really participate in any of the lobby night life aside from walking thru or stopping at the casino. On the last night we found the rooftop bar/restaurants and spend some time at the Tequilla bar (on the 10th floor). This is worth the trip on the elevator and had a great view. The bar tender was great and we had great service and a fun night. We only had one meal at the hotel 鈥?breakfast at the Veranda. It was very good but I found it expensive. We were able to eat offsite for 录 of the price. A great place across the street is call Mi Casita and was great for breakfast or lunch. They had excellent coffee. A walk down the beach is the Blue Dolphin which is an interesting outside bar that you can walk to for a very casual atmosphere (walk towards the big restaurant sign). In Old San Juan we had dinner at Caf茅 Puerto Rico, which was also very good. There are plenty of restaurants around the hotel within walking distance if you don鈥檛 want to pay hotel prices. The tours offered by the hotel seemed very overpriced. We rented a car one day and went to the rain forest on our own. It was a great day of exploring. We arranged for the car through the concierge and it was very easy and convenient. For less than $50 (car rental + gas) we did the rain forest and beach tour plus our own exploration. With a tour it would have cost $132.00 for two of us. At the rain forest we did two short hikes 鈥?one up Mt Britton and one down to a waterfall where you could swim. It was fun and it wouldn鈥檛 have been included in the tour. We also went to Old San Juan a few times. One time we went via cab - $32 round trip + tip and the other times we took the bus for a $1.00 total roundtrip for two of us. The bus is fine. The stop is outside the hotel. It does take 30 minutes longer than the cab but it鈥檚 an experience in itself. Old San Juan is nice walking tour that you can do on your own. The forts are worth checking out and there are good restaurants. The weather was hot and humid. It did rain every day that we were there but usually only for an hour or so. We were there in May 21-26 and it was not crowded at all. Overall, Puerto Rico was pleasant and an interesting vacation. The hotel atmosphere was nice, the service was ok, some employees were great and others could improve, and the prices on the premises were high. Again depending on what you鈥檙e looking for this hotel might be the right fit. My husband would have preferred to stay in Old San Juan and I would prefer the Conquistador so Wyndham El San Juan was a happy medium for us.

<Author>Temporary
<Content>Okay, but a little too expensive for mere mortals I was invited to a special conference in San Juan, Puerto Rico, and the conference activities took place in this hotel.The first thing I noticed when I got in the room was the air conditioner running at full blast. This was necessary in order to keep the tropical humidity from making the room a soggy mess. On the other hand, it was very cold and made sleep difficult at times.Also, the hotel is very close to the airport, and the jets taking off and landing were very loud. (The jet noise was especially unnerving three months after 9/11!)Other than that, I didn't find anything really wrong with the place. I didn't get to try the restaurants (always found better, cheaper food on the outside), but did enjoy some munchies and an adult beverage in the upper-story bar...There were some classy-looking (and probably expensive) shops selling jewelry, clothes, shoes, etc. in the lobby. There was also a small casino, where I won a few bucks playing video poker. Beware, there is a casino dress code in the evenings; people in shorts, etc. will be turned away.The conference itself kept me too busy to enjoy the beach, pool, and other resort features. However, I did get to sneak outside at times, and explore the neighborhood just outside the hotel. Safe and full of tourists (and a few bums hanging out around the liquor store). Be careful crossing the street, as there are few traffic lights in this area and traffic isn't always looking out for the lowly pedestrian....If you want to be adventurous, pay $.25 for the A5 bus to Old San Juanand save your $25 tourist cab fare for something fun. (The bus runs through a few dodgy areas, though, and the last runs leave around 9 p.m, so be prepared....)A final note: I was comped for my stay by the conference organizers, but I later found out that the cheapest room here is about $350 or so. Yikes! I didn't feel that this hotel was worth *that* much!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Wyndham is definitely 4 -star (but not 5 star) We were looking at tripadvisor trying to find a hotel for our 1st trip to P.R. I couldn't believe how people could give the same hotels both excellent and awful ratings. We were extremely unsure making our choice. We considered Wyndham Conquistador, the Westin Rio Del Mar, the Hilton Caribe, the San Juan Ritz and ended up picking the the Wyndham El San Jaun.Before I talk about the Wyndham ESJ, let me tell you what I learned about the different beaches in Puerto Rico. The Wyndham El Conquistador and Westin Rio Del Mar are about 1 hour from the airport/San Juan in an area called Rio Del Mar. The area around it is very poor and depressed so you are stuck on the property/their restaurants. I cannot tell you anything about the resorts themselves.The Wyndham El San Juan  the Ritz are in a section of P.R. called Isla Verde, which is literally 5 minutes from the airport. They all sit on this beautiful stretch of beach (no vendors, riff raff, etc) and you are a 15- minute ($16) cab ride to Old San Juan, which has GREAT restaurants. Plus, the area around the hotel has a lot of little restaurants as well as the fast food chains, so you are not stuck eating on the property.The Hilton Caribe sits in an area called Condado, which is about 1/2 way between Isla Verde and Old San Juan, so you would prob. get to San Juan in 5 minutes. BUT I noticed that it is in an area where the beach looked more rough/rocky - it didn't have the nice Isla Verde beach.I have stayed in some of the very best resorts in the world so I know the difference between good and outstanding. As for the Wyndham ESJ, it certainly provided a great resort vacation. The grounds, the lobby, the beach, the water sports, the pools, the restaurants, the landscaping, the entertainment, the service - all were typical class A resort. In fact, the entertainment/nightlife was especially great - there was tons of live music in the huge marble lobby on the weekends and there was certainly a buzz about it. We ate in Old San Juan almost every night and walked (less than 5 mins) to the local Caribbean restaurants for breakfast/lunch. It was totally safe and busy.The only drawback is that while the bathrooms are all refurbished, the rooms are fine/clean/standard but nothing special. Plus, they have to upgrade their HVAC system because while you can certainly freeze yourself as much as you want with your air-conditioning - there is always a slightly humid or clammy feeling. I asked the manager about this and he said the hotel was working on upgrading their HVAC system and was also renovating all the rooms starting this August so they should be done by next season.There were a couple of destination weddings there, lots of kids and teenagers. We were very pleased with our choice and actually after seeing other hotels we could have stayed at, we were thankful we had picked the Wyndham ESJ. The only better hotel would have been the Ritz - but there's not reason to pay for the Ritz since the ESJ is great. The Intercontinental, Hilton Caribe, etc., on the other hand, looked old/tired.

The balcony was large enough for a table and two chairs. We are Wyndham By Request members and received a very nice welcome gift upon arrival. As others have stated, you can't beat the nightlife at this hotel. The casino was great fun and very lively. They offered so many different entertainment options that we couldn't check them all out in one evening. A Latin dance band played in one of the lounges and another band performed in the casino. They also have a nightclub with DJ that caters to a younger crowd that was a lot of fun even though we're in our late 40's. The hotel offers 8 different restaurants in various price ranges. We ate dinner at The Ranch, which offered great views and good Mexican cuisine. The hotel grounds, pools and beach are beautiful and well maintained. The Wyndham El San Juan offers one of the nicest beach areas in San Juan. We truly enjoyed our stay and wouldn't hesitate to return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>People are overly critical of esj I stayed at the el san juan this past October. This was my third stay here and agree that for the most part many of the reviews have a grain of truth. The grounds are absolutely fabulous, the restaurants are top notch (but as most top notch restaurants in San Juan they are pricey), the staff are very eager to please, you can't beat the lobby for the nightlife. The best part of the hotel is the atmosphere. Here you feel that you are in a true Latin atmosphere with old fashioned luxury. Now for the bad part. The rooms do need some work. They are a bit run down but i disagree that they are dirty. During our stay the housekeeping staff were incredibly diligent even washing down the walls of the room. Unfortunately everything could use a good updating in the rooms which may give it a dirty feel. But they definitely were very clean and a reasonable size. The housekeepers were friendly and unlike many other 4 star hotels would make up the room almost immediately after we left and were very attentive. Although the rooms need work, i think the positives of the resort far outweigh the negatives for anyone thinking of staying in San Juan. My wife and I have stayed at the Ritz Carlton and have chosen the El San Juan instead so that we could get less of the generic luxury hotel feel that you get at the ritz.

<Author>etro
<Content>No Praise for Wyndham Anyone who has given this hotel a good rating must have been drunk their entire vacation. When I started staying at the El San Juan, it was managed by the Williams Hospitality Group, and it was, without a doubt, the most elegant hotel in the Isla Verde/Condado area. It was spotless, inside and out, and the service was warm and personal. Since Wyndham took over management, the hotel has changed for the worse. I was there in November, and I experienced the same check-in problems as other reviewers. I arrived 12:00 noon and finally got into my room at 5:00 P.M. The 'pager' sure was a waste of time. I have found the last few years that many of the employees have been rude. Surely no one cared that we waited all afternoon to get the room. In fact, when we complained at 4:30 P.M.,the front desk person said the hotel has until 5:00 P.M. to get the room ready. Rude? You bet. Our room was O.K., and when I spotted the coffee set-up, I was anxious to have a cup of coffee. By the way, Puerto Rican coffee is one of the best coffees in the world. When I looked closer at the coffeemaker, there was about a quarter of a pot of coffee left in the carafe, and it was molded! How long had that been sitting there? I lost my taste for coffee. I later requested a clean carafe, but believe it or not, that same carafe (with the molded coffee) remained in the room for the four days I was there - proof that the rooms aren't cleaned too often. Two years ago the concierge booked the wrong restaurant for my daughter and her husband, and shrugged and said, so go to the one I booked. Acouple of years ago my friends were at the pool area without their pool wrist bands, and were treated like criminals by the Security force. I could go on and on, but you get the idea. Maybe these misses don't seem too important, but I've never paid under $300.00 for a night at this hotel, and so I would expect much better treatment. Why return? It's like everyone says, the pool area and the lobby are great and there's always activity around. I guess management knows what the draw is, so they cut corners on customer relations and cleanliness. I took a walk to the Ritz Carlton during my trip and, quite frankly, it felt creepy, it was so quiet. By the way, one reviewer mentioned the beach being shared by the El San Juan and the Intercontinental. Well, actually the entire beach is public, so anyone can sit on the beach in front of either hotel.

<Author>TravelBeard
<Content>How sad! If a housing project had glass elevators, what would these look like? The answer to this, and other questions associated with the decline of a once great hotel can be yours if you were to choose to visit Wyndham's El San Juan Hotel. We checked in with a front desk agent whose demeanor was less five star hotel and more prison warden. Despite it being after 4p, we were told that our room was not ready. The agent, clearly allergic to smiling, provided a vibrating device that would prompt us to return to the front desk when the room was ready--a pager similar to those a Chili's patron gets when waiting for a table. As we went over to check our bags, another front desk agent, this one much more pleasant, rescued us, and had found us an upgraded room in the garden section.We proceeded over to the garden wing, in a lush banana tree and palm grove. Overall, the property was a bit overgrown with such foliage--a bit of manicuring would have gone a long way. The elevator, glass fronted, may have been the single most disgusting elevator in a hotel I've ever experienced. Filthy floors, smeared fingerprints on the glass, scratches on the metal, and for toppers, dead insects collected on the light cover on the elevators ceiling. Scuffed walls and unkempt tile floors provided a sequel in the hallways after we exited the famed elevator.In some hotels, you find your room with the room numbers posted outside the door. Here, you could also place your room by the unique stain on the carpet outside. The good news is that room was better than the trip there. The bad news is not by much. It was spacious, with a large balcony--the bathroom was also roomy. Everything would have benefited from a good cleaning, however, and dusting from the housekeeper appears to be a twice-annual luxury.I would have loved to have done a walk through the property with the general manager, who clearly has no pride in a hotel well kept. Wyndham showcases this hotel as a fine resort, but this once-proud San Juan landmark is disgusting on so many levels. How sad! Until Wyndham gets its act together here, best to stay away.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>3 1/2 Stars out of 5 Ok, heres the skinny on this hotel. I went wit my girlfriend from December 15th thru December 19th. The good parts about this hotel is that the workers are extremely nice, the restaurants are pretty good and the pool scene is amazing, not to mention the pool and jacuzies are open all night. My girlfriend and I brought a bottle of champagne to the jacuzzi at the late hours of the night and there was no problem. The casino is nice, although its not like Vegas or Atlantic City. The casino is small and don't expect to sit down at a $25 black jack table and get free drinks at the snap of your finger. I found the service slow and the dealers rude, but it was fun. There is also an nightclub and live music every night, although it is most busy Thursday - Sunday. The nightclub seems to be a lot of upper-class locals, while the live music is somewhat decent. The cigar rolling guy was an interesting touch to the lobby, which is decent. If anybody has been to a nice resort, you will know that just because the lobby is decent, does not make this hotel amazing by any stretch of the imagination. My girlfriend and I spent maybe an hour each night people watching over a drink. The location of the hotel is great, only 10 minutes from the airport and close to Old San Juan, for those that want to do some shopping. The only bad parts of the hotel are the rooms. As stated before, they have mold everywhere, the sheets are not changed unless requested and our shower water was never hot, only slightly warm. We're not huge complainers and since we were both there to sit by the beach and spend minimum time in the room, it didn't bother us as much as the families with kids. Over all, we had a great time and would return to this hotel, although if you can afford it, the Ritz is down the street and much nicer. Good luck!
