<Author>jessile
<Content>Friendly Service I booked my vacation 6 months out so I was constantly checking this website for updated reviews of guests who had just returned from their stay at this hotel. I had second doubts about placing my money here as I read review after review of guests who relayed their various dissapointments and dislikes of this Wyndham property. My friend and I opted to keep our reservations and checked in late on a Thursday night (September 2). The hotel was indeed bustling with people as the prior reviews read. I signed up for Wyndham by Request but was dissapointed when I got to my room and none of the perks that you are supposed to get were not there...no welcome beverage of choice...no snack of choice...no robes as requested, etc. So much for taking the time to fill out my requests! You could probably find similiar beds in a motel...the comforters must be at least ten years old...the decor (pictures on the wall, side tables, etc.) was fine as was the television hutch (which included a CD player inside). The bathroom in our room appeared updated (although some other reviews noted that they were old, outdated and needed a good cleaning!) and modernized with marble flooring and a long glass shelf along the wall above the sink. The one thing that I didn't like was that the bathroom entry way went up from the rest of the floor about an inch or two and I keep stubbing my toes! Our room overlooked a portion of the pool grounds and looked out over the ocean (6th Floor); I would recommend staying on this side of the hotel. Once your curtains are drawn, the view from the room was absolutely beautiful! Getting to the nightlife scene in this hotel (by the way, I'm 25 and my friend who I went with is 31)...I have read several reviews that Club Babylon was the spot to be at! We also chose this hotel based on the convenience of just going up to our hotel room after staying out late partying. A few notes to single people: The drinking age in Puerto Rico is 18 -- which means that you should plan on partying with a VERY young crowd almost all nights. Also, couples arrive together...being from Los Angeles, I was expecting to see the normal pack of girls and pack of guys arriving separately...not the case here. Guys and girls come arm in arm here! And boy do they love their own wild music! Thank God that the DJ did play a variety! The pool grounds are open 24 hours so that's cool and the beach outlet from the pool grounds has a security guard positioned, so that was a little comforting for those who desire to stroll the beach late at night or dare stay out long enough to watch the sun come up in the morning (and who wouldn't want to in Puerto Rico!?). I was starving reeeaaalll late one night and was glad to find that the hotel had 2 places that were open 24 hours. I had pasta at 4:00 a.m. and as hungry as I was, I didn't mind paying $20 for it and a soda! It definately wasn't worth the cost because it didn't taste that great but at the moment, it filled my craving so I can't really complain. Be sure to check out Tequila Bar  Grill on the 10th floor -- you can catch a great sunset view while sipping on your favorite drink. I can't tell you much about the casino because I didn't step one foot into it...but its a nice thing to have the hotel...just another one of the many things to do here. All in all, the staff was friendly, the checkout was easy, and the location was prime. If I may suggest....St. Thomas is so close to Puerto Rico that you should really get over to this magnificent island (and St. John is only a 15 minute fairy ride from there!)...we broke up our trip to include these two spots and it hurt to board a plane and come back to PR! As it turned out, the Ritz Carlton, where we stayed in St. Thomas, was cheaper than the Wyndham, and the grounds and atmosphere don't even compare! It was so peaceful and tranquil but yet the hotel was still close enough to those seeking nightlife! Wherever you decide to stay while in Puerto Rico, enjoy your trip to the latin country!

Apparently, they were doing some emergency work nearby and the electricity would be out until 6pm. Not a very good start especially after reading the reviews. We finally got into our (dark, not air conditioned) room, put on our bathing suites and heading to the pool (very nice pool and beach area!!!). Our room was clean and very large (ask to stay in either the garden suites or ocean view rooms they are the best-the tower rooms are supposedly horrible!). Long story short, we didn鈥檛 get electricity until 9pm we had to cancel our dinner reservations and couldn鈥檛 shower. We ended up heading to the tower having dinner at the pizza place in the hotel (very very good, but expensive) and drinking at the palm court (excellent selection of wine!). The next day we got the whole night comped (after some argument with the manager). All in all, it was fine. The place is what you make of it鈥he staff is pretty rude and not very helpful, but there were a few staff members that were excellent (bartender at the tiki bar is great!). The restaurants are very good, however very expensive. Old San Juan is overrated, but take a cab there ($16/way) and spend a few hours it鈥檚 worth it. The hotel has a great nightlife! It is definitely for a younger crowd. Make sure to spend a weekend there because all the good nightlife starts on Thursday. Best piece of advice: become a Wyndham by request member (it鈥檚 free) and get the free room upgrade. Go and enjoy yourself!! It鈥檚 worth it!

<Content>Beautiful Grounds, Rooms need an update I booked this hotel about 6 weeks prior to my arrival, and was concerned once I had read all the negative reviews. Walking to the garden, I was very impressed with the care in which the grounds were kept. The gentleman who showed us to our room was polite and informative. The room was large, with double sinks in the open bathroom, and a balcony overlooking the tropical foliage and one of the pools. At first glance, the room seemed lovely and clean, but a closer inspection revealed mold and rust and tiny insects. The sprinklers in the ceiling were caked in dust and dirt, the door stoppers were melting and caked in dirt, the bathroom had a bare lightbulb near the toilet. Plus, everything seemed damp all the time.The pools were really cool, but had leaves in them, and the whirlpools had all sorts of mold and chemicals along the edges. The beach was lovely, with tons of water sporting options. The food was really great all around, not a single complaint there. The waiters were friendly and quick, anticipating your needs before even calling on them. Just be sure to expect that the food will be expensive in the resort.Lobby was very lively, with live music and bars and the casino. Lot of fun!In sum, staff, security, grounds and food were fantastic. Rooms really, really need an update. Surrounding neighborhood is a bit shady. Even though I had a lot of fun, I will not stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Low-down Here is the low down. This hotel is great if you are looking for: 1. great nightlife and being the center of the action 2. fun place to people watch by the pool or by the beach 3. a heavenly poolside massage while coquis chirp in the background 4. a fun place to gamble 5. you are paying $175 or lessThis hotel is not for you if: 1. you are looking for quality hotel food (the restaurants are mediocre at best... touristy, bland and unoriginal. don't waste your time or money. old san juan (aguaviva and dragonfly) and the water club are the places to go for good food.) 2. you expect to be pampered and coddled by hotel employees 3. you are a light sleeper (a good portion of the rooms face the airport and it is very true that it sounds like an airplane landing in the room. the ritz carlton is no better in this respect) 4. you expect rooms to look very new and renovated 5. you are paying over $200 for a regular double roomIt's all about preferences and expectations, people. everyone goes on vacation with a different set of them. the ESJ is where i stay when i want a party vacation with my girlfriends and i want to blow off some steam at night (drinks at the lobby bar, wonderful food in old san juan, after dinner drinks at the water club rooftop, and dancing in the ESJ club), and alternate between sleeping on the beach and people watching by the pool during the day. when i come with my boyfriend, you'll find me at the water club, the el convento or on vieques.

<Author>LoriZ
<Content>Fun Time, Great Resort We went to the Wyndham El San Juan after 5 days on Vieques. Vieques was the quiet, relaxing part. And El San Juan the party part. Planned it so we arrived there on Friday, so we could have the weekend nights there. The lobby is huge, and gorgeous. Dark paneled wood, with 3 lobby bars, casino, Latin Dance club with live music, and disco. This is supposedly the most happenin spot in San Juan on weekends - with lots of locals coming by. Best part, with 2 kids along (7  14), didn't have to leave the resort to enjoy some of the nightlife. At one point, my husband and I just sat at a table in the lobby, Martini's in hand, people-watching. It really did give the impression of Havana during it's heyday. Good security - so only hotel guests could enter certain areas of the resort. We got a very nice room in newly renovated 3 story portion of the hotel. At first I was disappointed because I thought the main hotel was the better place, but room was nice where we were, more private and convenient to the pool. Grounds are beautifully landscaped, lush and clean. Even though one pool was being redone, we didn't miss it much. The other pool and several hot tubs were plenty and kept the kids happy for hours. If you want great, local food at reasonable prices and very reasonable breakfast, there is a restaurant called La Casita in little shopping center 3 blocks right as you exit the hotel. Also, the rainforest, El Yunque, is definitely worth a visit.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Anniversary "Surprise"! I booked a three night stay for my husband and I at the Wyndham ESJ for our 20th wedding anniversary (it was a surprise for my husband). Who would have guessed that the real surprise was going to be on me!!!! I called the Wyndham ESJ to make dinner reservations and set-up some in room surprises for my husband (for our arrival date and anniversary, August 27th). The receptionist told me that I should contact Wyndham by Request and become a member so that I could personally request exactly how I wanted our room set-up. I spent over 20 minutes filling out forms and requesting special items to be placed in the room. What a great idea...or so I thought!! When we arrived at the hotel, we went straight to the By Request desk (holding our membership card in hand). We gave them our membership card and waited as the gentleman punched in our number. I'm sorry, but we have no record of you in our computer we were told. You'll have to check-in at the main reservation desk. Okay, little bump in the road, nothing major, I thought, and we proceeded over to the reservation desk. The specialist confirmed our reservation and asked us to check the dates of our stay. Excuse me, I said, this isn't right. We are supposed to be staying three nights (27th - 30th). Oh, no, I'm sorry, but we've overbooked the hotel and your final night has been cancelled. SURPRISE!!!! Happy Anniversary!!! Of course my husband saw that I was slowly having a major melt-down, so he came to my defense. After several minutes and no resolution to the situation, she said they had given us a wonderful room with an ocean view...one of our best, to make up for the mix-up. While we waited for her to see what she could do about our reservation, or lack thereof, she gave us the key to our room and we decided to unpack and relax. Now, of course, I'm thinking at the price I'm paying, and the looks of the lobby (which was gorgeous), that our room would be wonderful (just as she described). If you call mold around the air conditioning vent, cigarette burns on the carpeting, and broken wood slats on the window wonderful, then this room was WONDERFUL!!! And, not to mention, the room smelled like dirty socks. If this is one of their best, I'd hate to see their worst. To make a long story short (if that's possible) we checked out the Intercontinental (a couple of doors down...where they were going to send us for our third night's stay). We ended up being so impressed by the staff and the hotel that we immediately booked three nights there instead. We returned to the Wyndham ESJ, cancelled our existing reservation, and headed back to the Intercontinental where our anniversary trip ended up much better than it started off. My advice to anyone considering the Wyndham ESJ....call ahead to make sure they didn't overbook and that you still have a reservation, or you too, might be SURPRISED!!!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall a very good experience for a party of 19 After reading some negative reviews on this site, we emailed ahead to the WyndhamByRequest manager. We were an extended family of 21 on a reunion. Our experience was quite smooth. We were all upgraded to the Garden lanai rooms near the pool on the same floor. The casino is one of the largest with a variety of games and we all won money. The restaurants can be pricey but by being in Isla Verde, you have the option to walk and eat closeby. Metropole, a local renowned restaurant, is within walking distance. There are also your usual American places like Burger King, Ponderosa Steakhouse, Wendy's, Outback Steakhouse, etc. and are cheaper options for breakfast, lunch or dinner. Our floor was a nonsmoking room but one room ended up smoking. With a complaint, the manager apologized and provided complimentary full breakfast vouchers. By the poolside, one day, our lunch order took 50 minutes. With another complaint, we got free drinks. The bigger pool was nice and the kids and adults had a good time - there is pool volleyball, a swim up bar, and the lounge chairs all have cushions. The beach is okay but the water is rough. We stayed close to the Wyndham just in case and experienced no trouble. We did hear the planes but it didn't really bother us. Wyndham was the happening place Saturday evening where people dress to the nines. After 7, there is a dress code but you can wear shorts and exit on the side without any commotion. Being close allows us to take a cab to Old San Juan for sightseeing and shopping, and to Condado, another nice area to visit. Overall, we had a good time and a smooth trip.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Avoid this hotel at all costs! My boyfriend and I stayed here for 5 days, 4 nights in June, 2003. We arrived at the hotel at 2:00 pm, and after waiting to check in at the front desk for 45 minutes, we were told that our room would be ready fairly soon. After checking back with the front desk numerous times, we were told at 5:30 that our room was finally ready. We retrieved our luggage from the bellboys, without so much as an offer to bring them up to our room. When we got to our room, we opened our sliding doors to reveal... a beautiful view of the parking lot and the airport runway. All we could hear for the next 5 days were airplanes taking off and landing. It was truly terrible. The room smelled like mildew, the walls looked dirty, as if they had not been painted in decades. We tried to make the best of the situation, as many often say, You don't spend your vacation in your hotel room. So we made our way down to the pool. And it is here, where the El San Juan slightly redeems itself... Slightly. The pool is beautiful, the grounds are very attractive. The beach, however, was not attractive at all. To your far right are decrepit, run-down local restaurants. As you walk onto the beach, you are immediately accosted by the chair man, who, like the rest of the El San Juan staff, immediately sizes you up in order to determine how much assistance he will provide you with. Apparently, my boyfriend and I did not seem to be wealthy enough or mature enough to garner much attention from this person, that is, until it came time to tip him. After he practically threw our chairs in the sand, he stood over me, waiting for his tip, and sucked his teeth in disgust after I handed him several dollar bills. This, I'm afraid, is a very common attitude amongst the staff at the El San Juan. Waiters and waitresses practically ignored us, and the concierge and the front desk staff sneered at us every time we came by with a request for information. We couldn't figure out if it was because we were not dressed in three piece suits or because we couldn't speak fluent Spanish, but for some reason, we were treated with not one iota of respect. The hotel has a dress code, where shorts are not permitted in the lobby area after 7 pm. I could understand this policy, as the El San Juan is a fairly fancy hotel, and offers a great deal in terms of nightlife, i.e., casino, cigar bar, clubs, etc. What I didn't understand was why, when we walked through the lobby in the afternoon in our bathing suits/shorts/coverups, we were stared at as if we were walking around naked. Now, understand, at night, we did dress up. We live in New York, and are accustomed to having to dress up in order to gain entry to finer restaurants, bars, clubs, lounges, etc. So we couldn't figure out why we were continually treated with such rude and unfriendly attitudes. Food was ok. I've had better. Lunch options at the grill beside the pool are limited, yet extremely pricey. We ate at two of the restaurants in the hotel, on the top floor, overlooking the beach. It was pleasant, but the food was still not worth the price we paid for it. I would not recommend this hotel to anyone I know. The service we received was completely awful. After the constant exposure to this rude and unfriendly staff, we even began to feel uncomfortable, as if we did not belong. My word of advice: Your money is better spent somewhere else.
